Suretyship for Kitabah Debt Invalid
Prohibition of suretyship for kitabah debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suretyship for kitabah debt and identify the reason for its prohibition.

Core Idea
Suretyship for kitabah debt is invalid because the slave's obligation is a personal commitment, not a transferable debt.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school: suretyship (kafalah) for the debt of kitabah is not permissible. The source text states this prohibition clearly, whether the would-be surety is free or a slave. Understanding this rule requires appreciating the unique nature of the kitabah contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Recognize that the act in question is suretyship (kafalah) for the wealth of kitabah (māl al-kitābah). The mukatib (slave under kitabah) owes this debt to his master.
2
State the Ruling
The ruling is clear: suretyship for this debt is not permissible (ḥarām). The text uses 'nahīṅ jā'iz' which indicates a prohibition.
3
Note the Scope
The prohibition applies regardless of the status of the surety: whether free or a slave. No distinction is made.
4
Understand the Reason
The debt of kitabah is not a regular financial debt; it is a personal obligation tied to the contract of emancipation. It cannot be transferred or guaranteed like an ordinary loan.
This is the underlying legal rationale (ʻillah) for the prohibition.
5
Confirm the Muftā Bihī
The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) in the Hanafi school is impermissibility, as stated in the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah texts.
Some other schools may differ, but within the Hanafi school this is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۵۰] (۳۳) نہیں جائز ہے کفالہ مال کتابت کا چاہے آزاد اس کا کفیل بنے چاہے غلام ۔ مکاتب نے کتابت کے لئے مولی کا قرض اپنے سر لیا۔ اس قرض کا کوئی کفیل بننا چاہے تو کفیل نہیں بن سکتا۔
(33) It is not permissible to be surety for the wealth of kitabah, whether the surety is free or slave. The mukatib has taken the debt of kitabah from the master upon himself. Whoever wants to become surety for this debt cannot become surety.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This is a standalone ruling that suretyship (kafalah) is not valid for the debt of kitabah. Kitabah is a contract where a slave agrees to pay his master a specified sum in installments to earn his freedom. The slave's obligation to pay is not considered a regular debt that can be guaranteed by a third party. Whether the would-be surety is free or a slave himself, the suretyship is invalid. The reason is that the kitabah contract is personal to the slave and master, and the slave's obligation is more akin to a personal commitment rather than a financial debt that can be transferred.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukātib): A slave who has a contract of kitabah with his master, working to pay for his freedom.
مال کتابت (māl al-kitābah): The money owed by the mukatib to his master under the kitabah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is suretyship for the debt of kitabah invalid?
A) Because the master does not accept
B) Because the slave cannot be sued
C) Because kitabah debt is not a regular debt; it is a personal contract
D) Because the surety must be free

Key Takeaway
Suretyship for kitabah debt is invalid because the obligation is personal to the mukatib and cannot be transferred to a guarantor.

Hawalah is Permissible for Debts
Opening the chapter on Hawalah with its definition and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of hawalah and identify its primary evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Hawalah transfers a debt to a wealthy guarantor; the creditor must follow him when referred.

This lesson opens the Hanafi chapter on hawalah (assignment of debt). You will learn the basic ruling of permissibility, the primary hadith evidence, and the key terminology that structures all later discussions in this chapter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of hawalah (transfer of debt). The ruling is permissible (mubah) for debts.
Note: Permissible means it is allowed but not obligatory. The hadith encourages following the wealthy guarantor, but does not command it.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar (RA) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The procrastination of the wealthy is oppression. And if you are referred to a wealthy person, then follow him.'
The hadith is reported by Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'follow him' indicates that the creditor may pursue the guarantor for payment. This shows that hawalah is permissible and that the creditor's right transfers to the guarantor.
The imperative form (فَاتَّبِعْ) implies permissibility, not obligation, in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the additional proof
The practice of Abu Qatada (RA) is cited: he took upon himself the debt of a deceased person, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted it. This supports the validity of hawalah even without the original debtor's consent in some cases.
This demonstrates that hawalah can be done with the consent of the guarantor and creditor, even if the original debtor is deceased or unable to pay.
5
Define the four key terms
The passage introduces four essential terms: muhil (original debtor), muhtal (creditor), muhtal 'alayh (guarantor), and mutammanal bih (the debt itself). Knowing these terms is critical for understanding all later rulings on hawalah.
These terms are used consistently throughout Hanafi fiqh in this chapter.

كتاب الحوالة

[۱۴۵۲] (۱) الحوالة جائزة بالديون

ضروری نوٹ حوالہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ دین اصل مقروض سے کفیل کی طرف چلا جائے اور اب صرف کفیل ذمہ دار ہو۔ چونکہ اس میں قرض دوسرے کی طرف حوالہ ہو گیا اس لئے اس کو حوالہ کہتے ہیں۔ حوالہ کا ثبوت اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر عن النبي الله قال مطل الغني ظلم واذا احلت على ملى فاتبعه ولا تبع بيعتين في بيعة (الف) ( ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی مطل الغنی ظلم ص ۲۴۴ نمبر ۱۳۰۹ار ابن ماجه شریف، باب الحواله ص ۳۴۴ نمبر ۲۴۰۴ / بخاری شریف ، باب الحوالة وهل يرجع في الحوالة ص ۳۰۵ نمبر ۲۲۸۷) اس حدیث میں حوالہ کرنے کا ذکر ہے۔ اور یہ بھی ہے کہ کسی مالدار کی طرف حوالہ کیا تو اس کا پیچھا کرنا چاہئے۔
اس باب میں چار الفاظ استعمال ہوتے ہیں اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے (۱) جو آدمی قرض کا ذمہ دار یعنی کفیل بنے کہ اب میں قرض ادا کروں گا اس کو محتال علیہ کہتے ہیں (۲) اور جس آدمی پر قرض تھا مدیون یعنی مکفول عنہ اس کو محیل، کہتے ہیں (۳) اور جس کا قرض تھا یعنی مکفول لہ اس کو محتال الہ یا محتال کہتے ہیں (۴) اور جس مال کا ضامن بنا یعنی ممکغول یہ اس کو متعمال بہ کہتے ہیں۔
[۱۴۵۲] (۱) حوالہ جائز ہے ین کا۔ جو قرض صحیح کسی آدمی پر ہو اس کا حوالہ کسی آدمی پر کرے تو جائز ہے۔ محتال علیہ یعنی کفیل کا اپنا مال ہے اس لئے وہ کسی کو بھی دے سکتا ہے (۲) اوپر حدیث گزری کہ کسی مالدار پر حالہ کیا جائے تو اس کا پیچھا کرنا چاہئے (۳) خود حضرت ابو قتادہ نے اپنے اوپر میت کا حوالہ کرتے ہوئے کہا تھا۔ فقال ابو قتادة صل عليه يا رسول الله وعلى دينه فصلى عليه (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا احال دین، المیت علی رجل جاز ص ۳۰۵ نمبر ۲۲۸۹) اس لئے ان احادیث کی وجہ سے حوالہ جائز ہے۔
Chapter of Hawalah. [1452] (1) Hawalah is permissible for debts. (Urdu commentary): Essential note: The meaning of hawalah is that the debt is transferred from the original debtor to a guarantor, and now only the guarantor is responsible. Because in this the debt is transferred to another, it is called hawalah. The proof of hawalah is in this hadith: From Ibn Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'The procrastination of the wealthy is oppression. And if you are referred to a wealthy person, then follow him. And do not make two sales in one sale.' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Bukhari). This hadith mentions hawalah. And it is also that if one is referred to a wealthy person, then one should pursue him. In this chapter, four terms are used. Their detail is: (1) The person who becomes responsible for the debt, i.e., a guarantor, saying 'I will now pay the debt,' is called muhtal 'alayh. (2) The person who owed the debt, the debtor, i.e., the one for whom guarantee was given, is called muhil. (3) The person whose debt it was, i.e., the beneficiary of the guarantee, is called muhtal lahu or muhtal. (4) The property for which guarantee was given is called mutamannal bih. [1452] (1) Hawalah is permissible. If a person has a valid debt on someone, and he refers it to another person, it is permissible. The muhtal 'alayh, i.e., the guarantor, has his own wealth, so he can give it to anyone. (2) The hadith above stated that if one is referred to a wealthy person, then one should pursue him. (3) Abu Qatada himself, when referring the debt of a deceased person to himself, said: 'Pray over him, O Messenger of Allah, and his debt is on me.' So he prayed over him. (Bukhari). Therefore, because of these hadiths, hawalah is permissible.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Hawalah (assignment of debt). It is a ruling statement with proof. The author first states the ruling: Hawalah is permissible for debts. The commentary then defines hawalah as the transfer of a debt from the original debtor to a guarantor, so that the guarantor becomes solely responsible. The proof is given from the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'The procrastination of the wealthy is oppression, and if you are referred to a wealthy person, then follow him.' This hadith indicates the permissibility of hawalah and that the creditor should pursue the wealthy guarantor. Additional proof is from the practice of Abu Qatada, who took upon himself the debt of a deceased person, showing that hawalah can be done without the original debtor's consent in some cases. The passage also defines the four key terms: muhil (original debtor), muhtal (creditor), muhtal 'alayh (guarantor), and mutammanal bih (the debt itself). This establishes the foundational vocabulary for the chapter.

Key Terms
حوالہ (hawalah): Transfer of a debt from the original debtor to another person (guarantor) who becomes responsible for payment.
محيل (muhil): The original debtor who transfers his debt to another.
محتال (muhtal): The creditor (the one to whom the debt is owed), also called muhtal lahu.
محتال عليه (muhtal 'alayh): The guarantor who takes over the debt and agrees to pay.

Key Takeaway
Hawalah is a permissible transfer of debt, proven by the hadith of Ibn Umar, and requires clear terminology for its parties.

Consent of All Three Parties in Hawalah
Condition for validity of hawalah: consent of all three parties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of consent for hawalah and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the muhil's consent.

Core Idea
A valid hawalah requires consent of debtor, creditor, and guarantor; the debtor's consent may be waived in necessity.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a hawalah (transfer of debt) depends on the consent of all three parties: the original debtor (muhil), the creditor (muhtal lahu), and the guarantor (muhtal 'alayh). This lesson explains the rationale behind each consent and examines an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the necessity of the debtor's consent, based on the example of Abu Qatada.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is hawalah (transfer of debt). The condition for its validity is the consent of all three parties involved.
The matn states: 'وتصح برضا المحيل والمحتال له والمحتال عليه'.
2
Define each party
Muhil is the original debtor, muhtal lahu is the creditor, and muhtal 'alayh is the person who accepts the debt (guarantor).
These terms are essential for understanding the ruling.
3
Understand the rationale for each consent
The commentary explains: the muhil may not want to owe a favor; the muhtal lahu may prefer the original debtor; the muhtal 'alayh must willingly assume the obligation.
Each party has a right to choose.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi exception
Some narrations (e.g., Abu Qatada's story) suggest the muhil's consent may not be required in special circumstances, such as when the debtor is deceased.
This is a legitimate difference within the school.
5
Apply the ruling
To determine validity, check whether each party consented. If any consent is missing, the hawalah is not valid (batil).
The mufta bihi position requires all three consents for a living debtor.

کیونکہ اس کو تو اچھا ہے کہ اپنا قرض کسی اور پر چلا گیا اور دوسرا آدمی ضامن بن گیا (۲) حضرت ابوقتادہ نے میت کا قرض اپنے اوپر لیا اور بغیر میت کی رضامندی کے لیا۔ اس لئے بغیر محیل کی رضا مندی کے حوالہ صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ محتاللہ کی رضا مندی کی ضرورت اس لئے ہے کہ قرض اس کا ہے۔ اور آدمی آدمی میں فرق ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ہو سکتا ہے کہ محتال لہ دوسرے آدمی یعنی محتال علیہ سے قرض وصول نہیں کرنا چاہتا ہو۔ اس لئے محتاللہ کی رضا مندی کی ضرورت ہے۔ اور محتال علیہ کی رضامندی کی ضرورت اس لئے ہے کہ اس کی رضا مندی کے بغیر وہ قرض کیسے ادا کرے گا؟ حضرت ابو قتادہ قرض ادا کرنے پر راضی ہوئے تب ہی میت کا قرض ان پر حوالہ ہوا۔
[1453] (2) And it is valid with the consent of the muhil, the muhtal lahu, and the muhtal 'alayh. (Urdu commentary): [1453] (2) Hawalah is valid with the consent of muhil, muhtal lahu, and muhtal 'alayh. If all three people agree, then hawalah is valid. Muhil is the debtor, muhtal lahu is the creditor, and muhtal 'alayh is the one who takes responsibility for paying the debt. The consent of the muhil is needed because it is possible he does not want to accept a favor from someone. So his consent is necessary. In some narrations it is said that his consent is not necessary. (Footnote): The Prophet said: 'The procrastination of the wealthy is oppression, and if you are referred to a wealthy person, then follow him, and do not make two sales in one sale.' Abu Qatada said: 'Pray over him, O Messenger of Allah, and his debt is on me.' Then he prayed the funeral prayer over him. (Page 323) Because (continuing commentary): because it is good for him that his debt is transferred to another and another person becomes guarantor. (2) Abu Qatada took the debt of the deceased upon himself without the consent of the deceased. Therefore, hawalah can be valid without the consent of the muhil. The consent of the muhtal lahu is needed because the debt is his. And people differ. So it is possible that the muhtal lahu does not want to collect the debt from another person, i.e., the muhtal 'alayh. Therefore, the consent of the muhtal lahu is necessary. And the consent of the muhtal 'alayh is needed because without his consent, how would he pay the debt? Abu Qatada agreed to pay the debt, only then the deceased's debt was transferred to him.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage presents the second ruling of the chapter: Hawalah is valid only with the consent of all three parties involved — the original debtor (muhil), the creditor (muhtal lahu), and the guarantor (muhtal 'alayh). The commentary explains the reason for each consent. The consent of the muhil is generally required because he may not want to be obligated to the guarantor. However, there is a narration that suggests it may not be necessary, based on the example of Abu Qatada who took on the debt of a deceased person without the deceased's consent. This indicates a difference of opinion. The consent of the creditor is necessary because the debt is his right, and he may prefer the original debtor over the guarantor. The consent of the guarantor is obvious, as he willingly takes on the obligation. The passage uses the example of Abu Qatada to illustrate the need for the guarantor's consent: Abu Qatada consented, so the transfer was valid. This ruling is a straightforward condition of validity, with some flexibility regarding the original debtor's consent in cases where it is not possible to obtain.

Key Terms
رضا (rida): Consent; agreement of the party without coercion.
محيل (muhil): The original debtor who initiates the hawalah.
محتال له (muhtal lahu): The creditor to whom the debt is owed.
محتال عليه (muhtal 'alayh): The person who accepts the transfer of the debt and becomes responsible for payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a valid hawalah requires the consent of all three parties—muhil, muhtal lahu, and muhtal 'alayh—with an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the necessity of the muhil's consent in cases of necessity.

The Effect of Hawalah and the Issue of Tawa
Ruling on the effect of hawalah and the dispute regarding recourse to the original debtor when debt is lost.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tawa in hawalah and explain the dispute with the Shafi'i school, citing the proofs from both sides.

Core Idea
If the debt is lost due to the guarantor's insolvency, the Hanafi school allows recourse to the original debtor; the Shafi'i school does not.

In this lesson, we examine a specific dispute arising in hawalah: what happens if the guarantor (muhtal 'alayh) becomes insolvent or denies the debt? The Hanafi school, relying on the principle that a Muslim's wealth should not be lost, allows the creditor to revert to the original debtor. The Shafi'i school, however, holds that the transfer is final. We will study the proofs and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the default ruling of hawalah
When hawalah is completed with consent, the original debtor (muhil) is freed from the debt; the creditor can only demand payment from the guarantor (muhtal 'alayh).
This is the baseline; the exception is tawa.
2
Identify the exception (tawa)
If the debt is lost (tawa) due to the guarantor's inability to pay, the creditor may revert to the original debtor.
Tawa is the key term; its definition is contested between the schools.
3
Define tawa according to Abu Hanifa
Tawa occurs in two scenarios: (1) the guarantor denies the hawalah and takes an oath, or (2) the guarantor becomes insolvent and this is proven.
Abu Hanifa's definition restricts tawa to proven loss.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school cites the athar of 'Uthman ibn 'Affan: 'There is no loss upon a Muslim's wealth.' This indicates that the debt should not be lost; the creditor can reclaim from the original debtor.
This is a qawl sahabi with zanni thubut and dalala.
5
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school cites the athar of Shuraih: 'If a man makes a hawalah and then [the debt] is lost, he cannot have recourse to the first.' This suggests finality of transfer.
Both schools rely on athar; the ikhtilaf is in preference and interpretation.
6
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, if the guarantor defaults, the creditor can still sue the original debtor. Under Shafi'i law, the creditor has no recourse against the original debtor.
This has significant practical implications in financial transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۵۴] (۳) واذا تمت الحوالة برئ المحيل من الديون ولم يرجع المحتال له على المحيل الا ان يتوى حقه [۱۴۵۵](۴) والتوى عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله

[۱۴۵۴] (۳) اور جب حوالہ پورا ہو جائے تو محل قرض سے بری ہو جائے گا اور محتال لہ وصول نہیں کرے گا محیل سے مگر یہ کہ اس کا حق تلف ہو جائے۔
تینوں کی رضامندی سے حوالہ مکمل ہو گیا تو محیل یعنی اصل مقروض قرض سے بری ہو جائے گا۔ اب اس پر قرض نہیں رہے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اس سے قرض منتقل ہو گیا۔ اور محتال لہ یعنی قرض دینے والا اب مجیل یعنی اصل مقروض سے قرض وصول نہیں کرے گا۔ ہاں ! اگر محتال علیہ یعنی کفیل اور ضامن سے قرض وصول ہونے کی امید نہ ہو تب محیل یعنی اصل مقروض سے قرض وصول کرے گا۔
حوالہ اس امید پر کیا تھا کہ قرض خواہ کو قرض ملے گا۔ اور جب نہیں ملا تو اصل مقروض ذمہ دار ہوگا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے ۔ ع عثمان بن عفان قال ليس على مال امرئ مسلم توی یعنی حوالة (الف) (سن للبیھقی ، باب من قال يرجع على المسيل لاتوی علی اما مال مسلم، ج سادس، ص ۱۱۷ نمبر ۱۳۹۱ ار مصنف ابن ابی شیته ۸۴ فی الحوالة ان يرجع فيها ، ج رابع ص ۱۳۳۶ نمبر ۲۰۷۱۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسلمان کے مال میں ضیاع نہیں ہے یعنی حوالہ میں ضائع نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اصل مقروض سے وصول کرے گا۔
امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ اگر چہ قرض محتال علیہ سے وصول نہ کر سکتا ہو پھر بھی مجیل یعنی اصل مقروض سے وصول نہیں کر سکتا۔ وہ حوالہ کی وجہ سے ہر اعتبار سے بری ہو گیا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن شريح في الرجل يحيل الرجل فيتوى قال لا يرجع على الاول (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ۸۴ فی الحوالة اله ان يرجع فیها، جرابع ، ۳۳۶، نمبر ۲۰۷۲۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ چاہے مال ضائع ہو نے کا خطرہ ہو پھر بھی اول یعنی اصل مقروض سے وصول نہیں کرے گا۔
ال التوى : حلق تلف ہونا۔
لغت
[۱۳۵۵ (۴) اور حق تلف امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دو معاملوں میں سے ایک سے ہوتا ہے، یا حوالے کا انکار کر دے اور قسم کھالے اور اس پر کوئی حاشیه : (الف) حضرت عثمان بن عفان نے فرمایا مسلمان کے مال پر ہلاکت نہیں ہے یعنی حوالہ میں ہلاکت نہیں ہے ( وہ محیل سے بھی وصول کر سکتا ہے ) ( ب ) حضرت شریح نے فرمایا آدمی حوالہ کرے پھر محتال علیہ پر ہلاکت آجائے تو فرمایا کہ اول سے وصول نہیں کر سکتا ( یعنی مجیل سے )۔
[1454] (3) And when the hawalah is completed, the muhil is freed from the debts, and the muhtal lahu does not have recourse against the muhil except if his right is lost (tawa). [1455] (4) And tawa according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him)...[Urdu commentary]: [1454] (3) And when the hawalah is completed, the muhil will be freed from the debt, and the muhtal lahu will not collect from the muhil unless his right is lost. When the hawalah is completed with the consent of all three, then the muhil, i.e., the original debtor, is freed from the debt. Now there will be no debt on him, because the debt has been transferred from him. And the muhtal lahu, i.e., the creditor, will not collect the debt from the muhil, i.e., the original debtor. Yes, if there is no hope of collecting the debt from the muhtal 'alayh, i.e., the guarantor, then he will collect from the muhil, i.e., the original debtor. The hawalah was made with the hope that the creditor would get his debt. When he did not receive it, the original debtor becomes responsible. (2) There is evidence for this in a tradition (athar): from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan who said: 'There is no loss upon a Muslim's wealth,' meaning hawalah. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) From this athar it is understood that there is no loss in a Muslim's wealth, i.e., it will not be lost in hawalah; rather, he will collect from the original debtor. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, if the debt cannot be collected from the muhtal 'alayh, even then he cannot collect from the original debtor. He has been freed from all aspects because of the hawalah. (2) There is an athar from Shuraih: 'Concerning a man who made a hawalah to another and then [the debt] was lost, he said: He cannot have recourse to the first.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) From this athar it is understood that even if there is a risk of loss, he will not collect from the first, i.e., the original debtor. (Lexicon): al-tawa means destruction/loss. [1355] (4) And loss of right according to Abu Hanifa occurs from one of two situations: either he denies the hawalah and takes an oath, and there is no [proof?]. (Footnote): (A) 'Uthman ibn 'Affan said: There is no destruction upon a Muslim's wealth, meaning in hawalah there is no loss; he can collect from the muhil. (B) Shuraih said: A man makes a hawalah, then the muhtal 'alayh faces destruction, he said: He cannot have recourse to the first (i.e., the muhil).
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage deals with the effect of hawalah and the concept of tawa (loss of the right to recourse). The ruling states that once hawalah is completed, the original debtor (muhil) is freed from the debt, and the creditor (muhtal lahu) cannot revert to him unless the debt is lost (tawa). The commentary explains that 'tawa' means the loss of the debt due to the guarantor's inability to pay. The Hanafi position, attributed to Abu Hanifa, defines tawa as two scenarios: either the guarantor denies the hawalah and takes an oath, or he becomes insolvent with proof. In such cases, the creditor can revert to the original debtor. This is supported by the athar of 'Uthman ibn 'Affan: 'There is no loss upon a Muslim's wealth,' meaning that the debt should not be lost; the creditor can reclaim from the original debtor if the guarantor defaults. The passage then presents the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that the original debtor is completely freed regardless of whether the debt is lost. He cites the athar of Shuraih, who ruled that one cannot revert to the first debtor after hawalah. The commentary thus presents an inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafi allows recourse to the original debtor in case of tawa, while Shafi'i does not. The Hanafi position relies on the principle that Muslim wealth should not be wasted, and the Shafi'i position relies on the finality of the transfer. The passage also includes a lexical note: al-tawa means loss or destruction.

Key Terms
توی (tawa): Loss of the debt due to the guarantor's inability to pay, defined by Abu Hanifa as denial with oath or insolvency with proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is one scenario that constitutes tawa (loss) allowing the creditor to revert to the original debtor?
A) The guarantor denies the hawalah and takes an oath
B) The creditor moves to another city
C) The original debtor becomes wealthy
D) The debt is paid in full

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits recourse to the original debtor if the debt is lost due to the guarantor's denial with oath or insolvency, based on the principle that Muslim wealth should not be wasted.

The Three Types of Sulh
Defines three types of sulh and supports permissibility with primary evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of sulh (compromise) in Hanafi fiqh and state the primary evidence for the permissibility of each, while distinguishing the valid forms from the invalid exception.

Core Idea
Sulh is permissible in all three forms—acknowledgment, silence, and denial—as long as it does not violate Islamic boundaries.

Sulh, or compromise, is a vital tool for resolving disputes without going to court. The Hanafi school categorizes it into three types based on the defendant's stance: admission, silence, or denial. This lesson dissects each category and the evidence from Quran and Sunnah that establishes their validity, while noting the one exception that invalidates any sulh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Definition
State the meaning of sulh as a contract of reconciliation to end a dispute, and note that it is the opposite of contention.
The text defines sulh in the opening line.
2
List the Three Types
Name the three categories: sulh with acknowledgment (iqrar), sulh with silence (sukoot), and sulh with denial (inkar).
Each type depends on the defendant's response to the claim.
3
Examine the Evidence
Locate the Quranic verse (4:128), the Hudaybiyyah hadith, and the general hadith 'al-sulh ja'iz bayn al-muslimin'.
The general hadith includes all three types, but excludes sulh that changes halal/haram.
4
Apply the Exception
Identify the invalidating condition: a sulh that makes halal haram or haram halal is not permissible.
This ensures that compromise does not override Islamic law.
5
Understand the Rationale for Silence and Denial
In cases of silence or denial, the defendant is giving his own property to avoid litigation, which is valid as a voluntary gift.
The defendant's willingness is key, not the truth of the claim.

١٤٢٠ ] (١) الصلح على ثلثة اضرب صلح مع اقرار و صلح مع سكوت وهو ان لا يقر المدعى عليه ولا ينكر وصلح مع انکار وكل ذلك جائز
کتاب الصلح )
ضروری نوں صلح کے معنی مصالحت کے ہیں۔ یہ مخاصمت کی ضد ہے۔ صلح جائز ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ وان امرأة خافت من بعلها
نشوزا او اعراضا فلا جناح عليهما ان يصلحا بينهما صلحا والصلح خير (الف) (آیت ۱۲۸ سورۃ النساء۴ ) اور حدیث ہے۔ عـن بــراء بن عازب قال صالح النبى المشركين يوم الحديبية على ثلاثة اشياء (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب الصلح مع المشرکین ص ۳۷۱ نمبر ۲۷۰۰) اس سے بھی پتہ چلا کہ صلح جائز ہے۔ اور ابوداؤد میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الله الصلح جائز بين المسلمين، زاد احمد الا صلحا حرم حلالا او احل حراما (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الصلح ص ۱۵۸ نمبر ۳۵۹۴) اس حدیث سے بھی صلح کے جواز کا پتہ چلا۔ [۱۴۶۰) (۱) صلح تین قسم پر ہے۔ اقرار کے ساتھ صلح اور چپ رہنے کے ساتھ صلح، وہ یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ نہ اقرار کرے اور نہ انکار کرے اور انکار
کے ساتھ صلح۔ اور یہ تینوں صورتیں جائز ہیں۔ صلح کی تین صورتیں ہیں، پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ مدعی نے دعوی کیا کہ تم پر میرا ایک ہزار درہم ہیں ۔ مدعی علیہ نے اقرار کیا کہ ہاں ہیں۔ لیکن ایک ہزار کے بدلے میں ایک گائے دے دیتا ہوں اس پر صلح کر لیں اور مدعی نے مان لیا تو یہ اقرار کے ساتھ صلح ہوئی۔ یا یوں کہا کہ ایک ہزار درہم ہیں لیکن آٹھ سو پر صلح کر لیں اور دو سو درہم چھوڑ دیں تو یہ بھی اقرار کے ساتھ صلح ہے اور بجنبہ صلح ہے۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ مدعی دعوی کرے کہ تم پر میرا ایک ہزار درہم ہیں، مدعی علیہ نے اس پر نہ انکار کیا اور نہ اقرار کیا خاموش رہا، پھر کہا کہ اس کے بدلے میں گائے دیتا ہوں اس پر صلح کر لیں اس پر مدعی نے مان لیا۔ یہ صلح مع السکوت ہوئی۔ اور تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ مدعی نے دعوی کیا کہ تم پر میرا ایک ہزار درہم ہیں ۔ مدعی علیہ نے انکار کیا کہ آپ کا مجھ پر کچھ نہیں ہے۔ بعد میں کہا کہ چلو اس کے بدلے میں ایک گائے دے دیتا ہوں ۔ مدعی نے مان لیا اس کو صلح مع انکار کہتے ہیں کہ انکار کرنے کے بعد صلح کر لے۔ یہ تینوں صورتیں جائز ہے۔
اوپر والی حدیث الصلح جائز بین المسلمین سے معلوم ہوا کہ صلح جائز ہے اور یہ حدیث مطلق ہے اس لئے اس میں تینوں قسم کی صلح داخل ہیں۔ یعنی حدیث تینوں قسم کی صلح پر دال ہے (۲) صلح مع السکوت اور صلح مع انکار کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ یہ چیز آپ کی ہے تو نہیں لیکن میں دعوی کے جھمیلے میں نہیں پڑنا چاہتا۔ اس لئے مال دے کر اپنی جان اور عزت بچانا چاہتا ہوں۔ اور مال مدعی علیہ کا ہے اس لئے وہ اس کو خرچ کر
حاشیہ : (الف) اگر کوئی عورت اپنے شوہر سے نافرمانی یا اعراض کا خوف کرے تو ان دونوں پر کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کہ آپس میں صلح کریں۔ اور صلح خیر ہے ( ب ) حضور صلح حدیبیہ کے دن مشرکین سے تین باتوں پر صلح کی (ج) آپ نے فرمایا مسلمانوں کے درمیان صلح جائز ہے مگر وہ مصلح جو حلال کو حرام کر دے یا حرام کو حلال کر دے۔
Book of Sulh. Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 2, page 322. Book of Sulh. [1420] (1) Sulh is of three types: sulh with acknowledgment, sulh with silence (where the defendant neither admits nor denies), and sulh with denial. All of these are permissible. ... The meaning of sulh is reconciliation. It is the opposite of contention. The evidence for its permissibility is the verse: 'And if a woman fears from her husband rebellion or aversion, there is no sin upon them if they make peace between them, and peace is better' (4:128). And the hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib: 'The Prophet made peace with the polytheists on the day of Hudaybiyyah on three things' (Bukhari). And Abu Dawud: from Abu Hurayrah: 'The Messenger of Allah said: Peace is permissible among Muslims.' Ahmad added: 'Except a peace that makes lawful what is unlawful or makes unlawful what is lawful.' (Abu Dawud). [1460] (1) Sulh is of three types: sulh with acknowledgment, sulh with silence (where the defendant neither admits nor denies), and sulh with denial. All three are permissible. ... The hadith 'al-sulh ja'iz bayn al-muslimin' is general and includes all three types. ... Marginal note: (a) ... (b) ... (c) ...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage introduces the book of Sulh (compromise or settlement) and defines its three categories. Sulh is a contract of reconciliation to end a dispute. Its permissibility is established by Quran (4:128), the Prophet's practice at Hudaybiyyah (Bukhari), and the general hadith 'al-sulh ja'iz bayn al-muslimin' (Abu Dawud) with the important exception that it cannot make what is halal into haram or vice versa. The three types are: (1) Sulh with iqrar (acknowledgment) – the defendant admits the claim but agrees to settle for a different thing or less amount. (2) Sulh with sukoo’t (silence) – the defendant neither admits nor denies the claim but agrees to a settlement to avoid litigation. (3) Sulh with inkar (denial) – the defendant denies the claim but nonetheless agrees to a settlement to end the dispute. All three are valid according to the Hanafi school. The commentary clarifies that in the latter two types, the defendant is giving his own property to avoid the hassle of litigation, not because the claim is true. This is permissible as long as the settlement does not violate Islamic legal boundaries.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A contract of reconciliation or compromise between disputing parties to end a conflict, often involving a settlement payment.
إقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment or admission of a claim by the defendant.
سكوت (sukūt): Silence of the defendant, where he neither admits nor denies the claim.
إنكار (inkār): Denial of the claim by the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid type of sulh according to the text?
A) Sulh with acknowledgment (iqrar)
B) Sulh with silence (sukoot)
C) Sulh with denial (inkar)
D) Sulh that makes halal into haram

Key Takeaway
Sulh is permissible in all three forms—with acknowledgment, silence, or denial—but never if it violates the boundaries of halal and haram.

Sulh After Silence or Denial: Fidya and Mu'awada
Explains dual nature of sulh after silence/denial with example and hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the legal nature of sulh 'an inkar from the defendant's perspective (fidya) and the plaintiff's perspective (mu'awada), and apply the Hanafi ruling that such sulh is valid without acknowledgment.

Core Idea
Sulh after denial is a ransom for the defendant, not an acknowledgment of debt.

When a defendant denies a claim, a settlement (sulh) may still be reached. In Hanafi fiqh, such a compromise has a dual nature: it is a ransom (fidya) for the defendant to avoid oath and litigation, but a compensation (mu'awada) for the plaintiff. This lesson unpacks that distinction and the proof from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its dual ruling
Determine the act (sulh after silence/denial) and note that it has two legal perspectives: defendant (fidya) and plaintiff (mu'awada).
The hukm level is ja'iz (permissible) for both.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited (Sahih al-Bukhari, hadith 2449) and understand how it encourages reconciliation even in cases of denial.
The hadith implies the wrongdoer often denies, yet resolution is urged.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves permissibility: the command to seek forgiveness (tahlil) applies even when the other party denies wrongdoing.
This shows that acknowledgment is not a condition for valid sulh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Contrast with schools that require acknowledgment for sulh to be valid. Hanafis allow it without acknowledgment as fidya.
The practical consequence: Hanafis enforce the settlement even if defendant later claims no debt was owed.
5
Apply the ruling
In a scenario where a plaintiff claims 1000 dirhams, defendant denies, then they settle for a cow: from defendant's side it is fidya, from plaintiff's side it is mu'awada.
The cow becomes the defendant's property (as if sold) but the underlying claim is not acknowledged.

اور چپ رہنے کے بعد صلح اور انکار کرنے کے بعد صلح دعی علیہ کےحق میں قسم کا فدیہ دینے کے لئے اور جھگڑا مٹانے کے طور پر ہوتی ہے۔ اور مدعی کے حق میں معاوضہ کے درجے میں ہے۔ مدعی نے دعوی کیا کہ تم پر ایک ہزار درہم ہیں ۔ مدعی علیہ اس پر چپ رہا یا انکار کر دیا۔ پھر ایک گائے پر صلح کر لی تو یہ صلح مدعی علیہ کے حق عن السكوت والانكار فى حق المدعى عليه لافتداء اليمين وقطع الخصومة وفي حق المدعى بمعنى المعاوضة [ ۱۴۶۴] (۵) واذا صالح عن دار لم يجب فيها الشفعة [ ۱۴۶۵] (٦) واذا صالح على دار وجبت فيها الشفعة. میں ایسا مانا جائے گا کہ مدی علیہ پر کچھ نہیں تھا۔ البتہ مقدمہ کے جھمیلے سے چھوٹنے کے لئے اور قسم کھانے سے بچنے کے لئے اپنا مال فدیہ کے طور پر دے دیا۔ حقیقت میں اس پر کچھ بھی لازم نہیں تھا۔ اس نے انکار کیا تھا یا چپ رہا تھا اور مدعی نے گواہ کے ذریعہ اس پر کچھ ثابت نہیں کیا ہے اس لئے حقیقت میں مدعی علیہ پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہوا۔ اور جو کچھ صلح کے طور پر دیا وہ اپنی جان چھڑانے کے لئے دیا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے کہ انکار کے باوجود دنیا میں بھائیوں سے صلح کر لینی چاہئے ۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الا الله من كانت له مظلمته لاخيه من عرضه او شيء فليتحلله منه اليوم قبل ان لا يكون دينار ولا درهم (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب من كانت له مظلمته عند الرجل فحللهاله هل سبین مظلمته ؟ ص نمبر ۲۴۴۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اس دنیا میں بھائیوں پر کئے ہوئے ظلم کو حلال کر لینا چاہئے ۔ ظاہر ہے کہ ظلم میں آدمی انکار ہی کرتا ہے۔ اس کے باوجود اس پر صلح کرنے کی ترغیب دی اس لئے انکار کے باوجود صلح کر سکتا ہے۔ اور مدعی کے حق میں معاوضہ کے معنی میں ہے۔ کیونکہ مدعی یہ سمجھ رہا ہے کہ میری چیز مدعی علیہ پر تھی اس کے بدلے میں اس کی چیز لے رہا ہوں۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کس پر بھائی کی جانب سے ظلم ہو اس کی عزت کے بارے میں یا کسی اور چیز کے بارے میں تو اس کو آج حلال کر لینا چاہئے ۔ اس دن سے پہلے کہ نہ دینار ہو اور نہ درہم ۔
And sulh after silence and sulh after denial, in the right of the defendant, is for ransoming the oath and cutting off litigation, and in the right of the plaintiff is in the meaning of a compensation. The plaintiff claimed: You owe me one thousand dirhams. The defendant remained silent or denied. Then they made sulh on a cow. So this sulh in the right of the defendant is from silence and denial, for ransoming the oath and cutting off litigation, and in the right of the plaintiff is in the meaning of compensation. [1464] (5) And if he makes sulh from a house, pre-emption is not obligated in it. [1465] (6) And if he makes sulh on a house, pre-emption is obligated in it. It will be considered that nothing was owed by the defendant. However, to escape the hassle of the case and to avoid swearing an oath, he gave his property as ransom. In reality, nothing was obligatory upon him. He had denied or remained silent, and the plaintiff did not prove anything through witnesses, so in reality nothing was due from the defendant. And whatever he gave as sulh, he gave to free himself. (2) In the hadith there is an indication that despite denial, one should make peace with brothers in this world. From Abu Huraira said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Beware! Whoever has a wrong against his brother, in his honor or anything, let him resolve it with him today before there is no dinar and no dirham.' (alif) (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: Whoever has a wrong against a man and seeks his forgiveness… hadith no. 2449). In this hadith, it is that oppression done to brothers should be forgiven in this world. Obviously, the oppressor usually denies. Despite that, encouragement is given to make sulh, therefore sulh is permissible despite denial. And in the right of the plaintiff, it is in the meaning of compensation, because the plaintiff thinks that his right was due from the defendant and he is taking the defendant's property in exchange. Footnote (alif): He said: whoever has a wrong from his brother concerning his honor or anything, let him resolve it with him today before the day when there will be no dinar and no dirham.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning sulh after the defendant's silence or denial (sulh 'an sukut or sulh 'an inkar). The author explains that such a sulh has a dual nature: from the defendant's perspective, it is a fidya (ransom) to avoid swearing an oath and to end litigation, implying the defendant is not actually acknowledging the claim; from the plaintiff's perspective, it is a mu'awada (compensation) because the plaintiff believes he is receiving what is rightfully his. The commentator clarifies with an example: the plaintiff claims one thousand dirhams, the defendant denies or stays silent, then they settle with a cow. In reality, no debt is established due to lack of proof, so the defendant gives the cow to be free from the lawsuit and oath. The author supports this with a hadith from Abu Huraira encouraging reconciliation even when there is denial, because the wrongdoer often denies. This hadith indicates that sulh is permissible even without acknowledgment. The ruling is that sulh 'an inkar is valid, though it functions as a redemption for the defendant, not a sale.

Key Terms
فدیة الیمین (fidyat al-yamin): Ransom paid to avoid swearing an oath; in sulh, the defendant gives property to avoid oath and litigation.
صلح عن انکار (sulh 'an inkar): A compromise settlement made after the defendant denies the claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the legal status of a sulh made after the defendant's denial of a claim?
A) Invalid because there is no consideration.
B) Valid as a sale if the defendant admits later.
C) Valid as fidya for the defendant and mu'awada for the plaintiff.
D) Valid only if the defendant takes an oath.

Key Takeaway
Sulh after denial is valid in Hanafi fiqh as a fiduciary arrangement (fidya) for the defendant and a compensative transaction (mu'awada) for the plaintiff, without requiring acknowledgment.

Ruling on Sulh After Iqrar and Istihqaq of Part
Ruling with example on sulh after admission when part is claimed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when part of the subject matter in a sulh based on iqrar is claimed by a third party, and explain why it is analogous to a sale.

Core Idea
Sulh after admission is like a sale — if part of the property is reclaimed, the defendant recovers proportionally.

This passage presents a key Hanafi ruling on compromise settlements. When a settlement is made after the defendant admits the claim, it is legally treated as a sale. Therefore, if a third party later proves ownership of part of the property, the defendant is entitled to a proportional refund of the compensation given. Through an example, the text illustrates how this principle works in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of sulh
The ruling applies specifically to sulh based on iqrar (admission). Without admission, the ruling differs.
2
State the ruling
If part of the musalah 'anhu (subject matter) is later claimed by a third party, the defendant recovers a proportional part of the compensation.
3
Trace the analogy to sale
The text explicitly compares sulh after iqrar to a sale. In a sale, if part of the sold item is claimed, the buyer recovers part of the price. Similarly here.
The 'illa is the transfer of ownership for compensation.
4
Apply to the example
Work through the example: Umar admits the house belongs to Zaid, gives a cow in sulh, then half the house is claimed by a third party. Umar recovers half the cow from Zaid.
The proportional recovery is based on the fraction of the property claimed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلح
[۱۴۶۶] (۷) واذا كان الصلح عن اقرار فاستحق بعض المصالح عنه رجع المدعى عليه بحصة ذلك من العوض
ہوگا۔
مدعی اس گھر کو اپنے ہزار درہم کے بدلے لے رہا ہے۔ اس مدعی کے حق میں گھر کو ہزار درہم کے بدلے خرید نا پایا گیا اس لئے گھر میں شفعہ
اصول اوپر گزر گیا۔
[۱۴] (۷) اگر اقرار کے بعد صلح ہوئی ہو پھر مسحق نکل گیا صلح کی چیز کے بعض حصے میں تو واپس لے لے مدعی علیہ اس حصے کے موافق عوض
ہے۔
اس مسئلہ کو مثال سے سمجھیں۔ مثلا عمر کے قبضہ میں ایک مکان ہے۔ زید مدعی نے دعوی کیا کہ یہ مکان میرا ہے عمر مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ ہاں ایسا ہی ہے۔ پھر ایک گائے دے کر صلح کر لی۔ پھر بعد میں مکان جو مصالح عنہ تھا یعنی جس کی وجہ سے صلح ہوئی تھی اس میں سے آدھا حصہ دوسرے کا نکل آیا تو عمر زید سے اپنی دی ہوئی گائے کا آدھا حصہ واپس لے گا۔ صلح کی تو یہ خرید وفروخت کی طرح ہو گئی۔ اس لئے مبیع یا شمن کا مستحق نکل گیا تو سامنے والے سے وصول کرے گا۔ یہاں مکان کا آدھا حصہ مستحق نکل گیا تو گائے جو اس کی قیمت تھی اس کا آدھا زید سے واپس لے گا۔
سوال یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اقرار کے بعد صلح بیع کی طرح ہے۔
Book of Sulh. [1466] (7) And if the sulh was based on admission, and then part of the subject matter is claimed (by a third party), the defendant recovers the proportional share of the compensation. It will be. The claimant is taking this house in exchange for his thousand dirhams. For this claimant, buying the house for a thousand dirhams is established, so shuf'ah in the house [principle has passed earlier]. [14] (7) If sulh was made after admission, then a creditor (mustahiq) appeared in some part of the subject matter of sulh, then the defendant recovers the corresponding part of the compensation. Understand this issue with an example: For example, there is a house in Umar's possession. Zaid, the claimant, claimed that this house is mine. Umar, the defendant, said yes, that is so. Then he made sulh by giving a cow. Later, half of the house which was the subject matter (musalah 'anhu) i.e. for which the sulh was made, turned out to be someone else's. So Umar will recover half of the cow he gave from Zaid. Since the sulh became like a sale. Therefore, if the sold item or the price is claimed by a third party, he (the defendant) will recover from the other party. Here half of the house was claimed, so half of the cow which was its price, he will recover from Zaid. Question: This issue is based on the principle that sulh after admission is like a sale.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage begins by presenting a ruling from the Hanafi school on compromise (sulh) when it is based on an admission (iqrar) by the defendant. The ruling states that if after the sulh, a third party successfully claims part of the subject matter (the property that was the subject of the dispute), then the defendant (who made the admission and gave compensation) has the right to recover from the claimant a proportional part of the compensation he paid. This is because when sulh is based on admission, it is treated like a sale (bay'): the claimant buys the property from the defendant in exchange for the compensation. If part of the property is later found to belong to someone else, the sale is partially invalid, and the buyer (the claimant) must return part of the price. The commentary then provides a concrete example: Umar admits that the house belongs to Zaid, then they settle by Umar giving a cow. Later, half the house is claimed by a third party. Umar gets back half the cow from Zaid. The text emphasizes that the underlying principle is that sulh after admission is analogous to a sale.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A compromise or settlement where the claimant waives his claim in exchange for compensation from the defendant.
اقرار (iqrar): Admission by the defendant that the claimant's claim is true.
مستحق (mustahiq): A third party who proves ownership of the property that was part of the sulh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sulh based on admission (iqrar), if half of the disputed property is later claimed by a third party, what is the defendant entitled to?
A) He loses the entire compensation.
B) He recovers half of the compensation from the claimant.
C) He recovers half of the compensation from the third party.
D) He cannot recover anything because the sulh is final.

Key Takeaway
When sulh is based on admission, it is treated like a sale, so the defendant recovers proportional compensation if part of the subject matter is claimed.

Ruling on Sulh After Silence or Denial with Istihqaq
Ruling on sulh after silence/denial with istihqaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when sulh is made after the defendant's silence or denial and the property is later claimed by a third party, and apply the analogy to sale.

Core Idea
Sulh after denial is like a sale of immunity; if the property is claimed, the compensation must be returned.

This passage builds on the previous ruling on sulh after admission. Here, the sulh is based on the defendant's silence or denial. The Hanafi school analogizes this sulh to a sale: the claimant 'buys' the defendant's immunity from litigation by giving compensation. If a third party later proves ownership, the purpose of the sulh fails, and the compensation goes back to the defendant. The claimant must then pursue the third party.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The sulh occurs after the defendant's silence (sukut) or denial (inkar). The defendant gives compensation to the claimant to drop the case.
Silence is treated like denial here.
2
Determine the consequence of a third party claim
If the entire disputed property is later claimed by a rightful owner, the original claimant must return the full compensation to the defendant and then sue the third party.
The defendant is not responsible for the third party.
3
Apply the partial claim rule
If only part of the property is claimed, the claimant returns a proportional part of the compensation and pursues that part against the third party.
The example: half the house claimed → half the cow returned.
4
Understand the analogy to sale
The sulh is treated like a sale of the disputed property or the claim itself. If the seller's title fails (third party claim), the sale is rescinded and the price returned.
This qiyas is explicit in Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۶۷] (۸) واذا وقع الصلح عن سكوت او انكار فاستحق المتنازع فيه رجع المدعى بالخصومة ورد العوض وان استحق بعض ذلک رد حصته
ورجع بالخصومة فيه
[۸] (۸) اگر صلح واقع ہو چپ رہنے کے بعد یا انکار کے بعد پھر متنازع فیہ چیز کا کوئی حقدار نکل آئے تو مدعی مقدمہ کر کے وصول کرے گا۔ اور عوض واپس کرے گا۔ اور اگر اس میں سے بعض کا مستحق نکل گیا تو مقدمہ سے اس میں وصول کرے گا۔
اس مسئلہ کو بھی مثال سے سمجھیں۔ مثلا عمر کے قبضہ میں ایک مکان تھا۔ زید نے دعوی کیا کہ یہ مکان میرا ہے۔ عمر اس پر چپ رہایا انکار کیا۔ بعد میں عمر مدعی علیہ نے گائے دے کر صلح کر لی۔ اس کے بعد مکان کسی اور کا مستحق نکل گیا تو عمر مدعی علیہ زید مدعی سے اپنی گائے واپس لے گا اور زید در گی اب مستحق سے مقدمہ کر کے اس کے استحقاق کو ختم کرائے گا یا وہ حقدار کو حق دے گا۔
عمر مدعی علیہ اگر چہ چپ رہا تھا یا انکار کیا تھا لیکن اس نے زید کو مکان کے بدلے گائے اس لئے دی تھی کہ مکان کا کوئی حقدار نہ نکلے اور مکان بغیر خصومت کے اس کے پاس موجود رہے۔ یہاں تو حقدار بھی نکل گیا اور خصومت میں بھی پڑنا پڑا جس کی وجہ سے گائے دینے کا کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہوا۔ اس لئے زید سے گائے واپس لے گا۔ اور اب زید مقدار سے نمٹیگا ۔ کیونکہ حقدار اب مدعی علیہ عمر کے درجے میں ہو گیا۔ اس لئے اس سے خصومت کر کے یا اپنا حق واپس لے گا یا قاضی فیصلہ کرے گا تو اس کا حق حقدار کے پاس جائے گا (۲) یہاں بھی بیچ کی طرح
معاملہ ہو جائے گا اور عمر کی بیع (مکان) سالم نہیں رہا اس لئے اپنی قیمت گائے زید سے واپس لے گا۔
اور آدھا مکان مستحق نکلا تھا تو آدھی گائے عمر کو واپس دے گا ۔ اور آدھا مکان زید مستحق سے مقدمہ کر کے واپس لے گا۔
[1467] (8) And if the sulh occurs based on silence or denial, and then the subject of dispute is claimed (by a third party), the claimant (who brought the lawsuit) pursues the claim and returns the compensation; and if some of that is claimed, he returns its portion. And he pursues the claim therein. [8] (8) If sulh occurs after remaining silent or after denial, then a rightful claimant of the disputed thing appears, then the claimant (original plaintiff) will file a lawsuit and recover (from the third party), and will return the compensation. And if some of it is claimed, he will recover his share through a lawsuit. Understand this issue also with an example: For example, there was a house in Umar's possession. Zaid claimed that this house is mine. Umar remained silent or denied. Later, Umar, the defendant, made sulh by giving a cow. After that, the house was claimed by someone else. Then Umar, the defendant, will take back his cow from Zaid, the claimant, and Zaid will now file a lawsuit against the claimant (third party) to terminate his claim or give him his right. Umar, the defendant, although he remained silent or denied, gave the cow to Zaid in exchange for the house so that no rightful claimant would appear and the house would remain with him without dispute. Here, a rightful claimant did appear, and he had to enter into litigation, due to which there was no benefit in giving the cow. Therefore, he will take back the cow from Zaid. And now Zaid will deal with the third party, because the third party has become like the defendant Umar. So he will either file a lawsuit against him and take back his right, or the judge will decide, and his right will go to the rightful claimant. (2) Here too, the matter will be like a sale, and Umar's sale (of the house) did not remain intact, so he will take back his price, the cow, from Zaid. And if half the house was claimed, then he will give back half the cow to Umar, and half the house, Zaid will take back from the claimant through litigation.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage presents the second major ruling on sulh: when the sulh is based on the defendant's silence or denial (not admission). In this case, the claimant (who brought the original suit) is considered to have 'purchased' the defendant's immunity from litigation in exchange for the compensation. If later a third party proves ownership of the disputed property, the original defendant can reclaim his compensation from the claimant. The claimant cannot keep both the property and the compensation; he must refund the compensation and then go after the third party for his rights. The commentary explains the rationale: the defendant gave the compensation precisely to avoid any future claim and litigation. Since the claim materialized, the purpose failed, so the compensation goes back. The example clarifies that if only part is claimed, proportional recovery applies.

Key Terms
سكوت (sukut): Silence by the defendant when faced with a claim, implying neither admission nor denial.
انكار (inkar): Denial by the defendant of the claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If sulh is made after the defendant's denial, and later the entire disputed property is claimed by a third party, what must the original claimant do?
A) Keep the compensation and fight the third party.
B) Refund the compensation to the defendant and pursue the third party.
C) Keep the compensation and abandon the property.
D) Only refund part of the compensation.

Key Takeaway
In sulh after silence or denial, if the property is later claimed, the compensation is returnable, and the claimant must pursue the third party.

Sulh for Unspecified Claim and Partial Istihqaq
Ruling on sulh after unspecified claim and partial estihqaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that no refund is due when part of the sulh property is claimed, distinguishing between partial and total istihqaq.

Core Idea
An unspecified claim after sulh protects against partial refund: the claim is assigned to the remainder.

This passage addresses a subtle scenario in sulh (compromise) law: when a claimant asserts an unspecified right in a property, then settles for a counterpayment, and later a third party proves ownership over part of that property. Should the defendant recover part of the payment? The Hanafi ruling hinges on reconciling the parties' statements: unless the entire property is lost, the claimant's unspecified claim can be interpreted as limited to what remains with the defendant. This prevents unjust enrichment while preserving the validity of the sulh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Start by identifying the three parties: claimant (unspecified right in a house), defendant (who gives something in sulh), and a third party who later claims part of the house. Note that the claimant did not specify the quantum of his right.
The key is the lack of specification.
2
Apply the principle of reconciliation (tawfiq)
Apply the Hanafi principle that if the statements of claimant and defendant can be reconciled, they should be. Here, the claimant's vague claim can be interpreted as referring to the portion of the house that remains with the defendant after the third party's claim.
This avoids invalidating the sulh.
3
Distinguish between partial and total istihqaq
If only part of the house is claimed, the claimant can plausibly say 'that remaining part was my right, and I settled for it.' Thus, the sulh stands, and no refund is due. If the entire house is claimed, the claimant had no right at all, so the defendant recovers the full compensation.
Total istihqaq nullifies the basis of the claim.
4
Derive the ruling
Conclude: for partial istihqaq, the defendant recovers nothing; for total istihqaq, the defendant recovers the entire compensation.
This ruling is specific to unspecified claims; specified claims may lead to proportional refund.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۲۸] (۹) وان ادعى حقا في دار ولم يبينه فصولح من ذلك على شيء ثم استحق بعض الدار لم يرد شيئا من العوض لان دعواه يجوز انيكون فيما بقی
واذا استحق الكل رد العوض
(۹) اگر مدعی نے گھر میں حق کا دعوی کیا اور اس کی تفصیل بیان نہیں کی ۔ پس صلح کی اس کے بدلے میں کسی چیز پر ، پھر مستحق نکل گیا بعض گھر کا تو عوض میں سے کچھ واپس نہین کرے گا۔ اس لئے کہ اس کا دعوی جائز ہے کہ فیما بھی مین ہو۔ مثلا زید نے عمر سے کہا کہ تمہارے قبضے کے گھر میں میراحق ہے۔ لیکن کتنا حق ہے یہ بیان نہیں کیا۔ پھر عمر نے زید کو گائے دے کر صلح کی۔ بعد میں اس مکان میں کسی کا کچھ حق نکل گیا تو عمر زید سے گائے واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ کیونکہ جو کچھ مکان میں سے عمر کے پاس باقی رہ گیا ہے زید کہ سکتا ہے کہ اتنا ہی حق میرا تھا جو تمہارے پاس رہ گیا ہے اور اسی پر صلح کر کے گائے لی ہے ۔ ہاں اگر پورا مکان کسی کا مستحق نکل گیا تو عمر اب زید سے گائے واپس لے سکتا ہے ۔ کیونکہ جب پورا مکان کسی کا حق نکل گیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ زید کا تھوڑا حصہ بھی مکان میں نہیں تھا اور اس نے عمر سے جو گائے کی تھی وہ بغیر کسی حق کے لی تھی ۔ اس لئے عمر زید سے اپنی دی ہوئی گائے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔
یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اگر مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کی باتوں میں جوڑ پیدا ہو سکتا ہو تو کر دیا جائے گا اور نہ بعد میں فیصلہ ہوگا ۔
[1428] (9) And if he claimed a right in a house and did not specify it, and then he made a sulh for something in exchange, then part of the house is claimed (by a third party), he does not return anything of the compensation, because it is possible that his claim was in what remains. And if the whole is claimed, he returns the compensation. (9) If the claimant claimed a right in a house without specifying it, then he made a sulh for something in exchange, then a rightful claimant appeared for part of the house, he will not return anything of the compensation, because it is possible that his claim was in what remains. For example, Zaid said to Umar, 'I have a right in the house in your possession,' but he did not state how much right. Then Umar gave a cow and made sulh. Later, some right of someone else appeared in the house. Then Umar cannot take back the cow from Zaid, because what remains of the house with Umar, Zaid can say that this much was my right which remains with you, and on that I made sulh and took the cow. Yes, if the entire house is claimed by someone else, then Umar can take back the cow from Zaid, because when the entire house is proven to be someone else's right, it becomes known that Zaid had no share at all in the house, and he took the cow from Umar without any right. Therefore, Umar can take back the cow he gave. This issue is based on the principle that if the statements of the claimant and defendant can be reconciled, they should be, and no further decision is made.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage addresses a nuance: when the claimant asserts a right in a property but does not specify its extent (e.g., 'I have a right in this house' without saying it is half or quarter). After sulh, if a third party claims part of the property, the defendant cannot recover any compensation from the claimant because the claimant's unspecified claim could be in the remaining portion that the defendant still holds. The claimant can argue that his claim was exactly that part. However, if the entire property is claimed by the third party, then the claimant had no right at all, so the defendant can recover the full compensation. The underlying principle is that when the statements can be reconciled, they are given effect to preserve the validity of the sulh.

Key Terms
لم يبينه (lam yubayyinhu): The claimant did not specify the quantum or nature of his right.
استحق (istihqaq): A third party proves superior right (ownership or claim) over the property.
عوض (iwad): The consideration given in exchange for the sulh (e.g., a cow).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A claimant says to the defendant: 'I have a right in your house' without specifying. They settle for a sheep. Later, a third party shows they own half the house. What is the ruling?
A) The defendant gets the sheep back.
B) The defendant gets half the sheep back.
C) The defendant gets nothing back.
D) The sulh is void.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling protects the validity of sulh for unspecified claims by allowing the claim to be assigned to the remaining portion when part of the property is subsequently claimed.

Scope of Permissible Sulh in Various Claims
Statement on scope of permissible sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the types of claims where sulh is permissible and identify the one claim where sulh is invalid, according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sulh is valid for property, usufruct, and injury claims, but never for hadd punishments.

This passage from the matn outlines the scope of valid sulh (compromise). The Hanafi school permits sulh in nearly all financial and personal injury claims, but draws a firm line at claims involving hadd punishments. Understanding this scope is essential for structuring out-of-court settlements in Islamic legal practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four permissible categories
From the text, list the types of claims where sulh is permissible: property (amwal), usufruct (manafi'), intentional injury (jinaayat al-'amd), and unintentional injury (jinaayat al-khata').
These cover most financial and tort disputes.
2
Identify the prohibited category
Note the single exception: claims involving hadd (fixed punishments). The text explicitly says 'لا يجوز من دعوى الحدود'.
Hadd punishments are rights of Allah that cannot be privately compromised.
3
Understand the legal transformation in each case
The commentary explains that sulh in property functions like a sale, in usufruct like a lease (ijarah), and in injuries it replaces qisas or modifies diyah.
The nature of sulh adapts to the underlying claim.
4
Recognize the underlying rationale
Hadd punishments are excluded because they are rights of Allah, whereas other claims involve private rights of individuals that can be waived or negotiated.
This distinguishes between divine and personal claims.

[۱۴۶۹] (۱۰) والصلح جائز من دعوى الاموال والمنافع وجناية العمد والخطا
ولا يجوز من دعوى الحدود
(۱۰) صلح جائز ہے مال کے دعوی سے اور منافع کے دعوی سے ۔ جنایت عمد اور جنایت خطا کے دعوی سے۔ اور نہیں جائز ہے حد کے
دعوی سے۔
کسی نے مال کا دعوی کیا۔ اس کے بدلے میں کچھ دے کر صلح کر لی تو جائز ہے۔ اور یہ بیچ کے درجے میں ہوگی۔ یا منافع کا کسی نے دعوی کیا اور اس کے بدلے میں کچھ دے کر صلح کرلی تو جائز ہے۔ اور یہ صلح اجارہ کے درجے میں ہوگی۔ ان دونوں کی دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ جنایت محمد کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کسی نے جان بوجھ کر کسی کا عضو کاٹ دیا جس کی وجہ سے اس پر عضو کاٹنے کا قصاص تھا۔ اس قصاص کے بدلے میں دونوں نے مال پر صلح کر لی تو جائز ہے۔ اور جنایت خطا کی صورت یہ ہے کہ غلطی سے کسی نے کسی کا عضو کاٹ دیا جس کی وجہ سے اس
پر دیت کا مال واجب تھا۔ لیکن بعد میں قاطع اور مقطوع نے کم مال پر صلح کرلی تو یہ جائز ہے۔
[1469] (10) And sulh is permissible from claims of property, usufruct, intentional injury, and unintentional injury. And it is not permissible from claims of hadd (fixed punishments). (10) Sulh is permissible from claims of property and from claims of usufruct. From claims of intentional injury and unintentional injury. And it is not permissible from claims of hadd. Someone claimed property; he made sulh by giving something in exchange, so it is permissible. And this will be in the category of sale. Or someone claimed usufruct and made sulh by giving something in exchange, so it is permissible. And this sulh will be in the category of hire (ijarah). The proof for both has passed earlier. The meaning of intentional injury (jinaayat 'amd) is that someone deliberately cut off someone's limb, due to which there was qisas (retaliation) for cutting the limb. They made sulh on money in exchange for that qisas, so it is permissible. And the case of unintentional injury (jinaayat khata') is that someone mistakenly cut off someone's limb, due to which diyah (blood money) was obligatory. But later the cutter and the cut person made sulh on less money, so this is permissible.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage provides a general statement on the scope of valid sulh. Sulh is permissible for claims involving property (mal), usufruct (manafi'), intentional injury ('amd), and unintentional injury (khata'). In these cases, sulh functions like a sale (bay') or a lease (ijarah) as appropriate. However, sulh is not permissible for claims involving hadd punishments, as those are rights of Allah that cannot be compromised. The text gives examples: for property claims, sulh is like a sale; for usufruct claims, like an ijarah; for intentional injury, sulh can replace qisas with monetary compensation; for unintentional injury, sulh can reduce the diyah amount. The proofs for the permissibility of such sulh are referenced as having been mentioned earlier in the text.

Key Terms
جنایة العمد (jinaayat al-'amd): Intentional harm or injury that would normally require qisas.
جنایة الخطأ (jinaayat al-khata'): Unintentional harm that requires diyah (financial compensation).
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for crimes like theft, zina, etc., which cannot be compromised.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Usufruct claims

Key Takeaway
Sulh is a broad instrument in Hanafi fiqh, valid for all claims except hadd punishments.

Settlement When Part of Property Is Taken by Rightful Owner
Ruling on consideration return when part of settled property is taken

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether consideration must be returned in a settlement when part of the settled property is taken by a rightful owner, and explain the reasoning based on the possibility of reconciling the unspecified claim with the remaining property.

Core Idea
If part of the settled property is taken, the settlement stands; only if the entire property is taken must the consideration be returned.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the chapter of Sulh (settlement). When a person claims an unspecified right in a property and settles for a consideration, what happens if later part of that property is found to belong to someone else? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer: the settlement remains valid for the remaining portion because the unspecified claim can be plausibly interpreted as applying only to what remains. This ruling illustrates the broader principle of reconciling the statements of disputing parties wherever possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage to understand the three parties: the claimant (who claims an unspecified right in a house), the defendant (who settles by giving a cow), and the later-appearing rightful owner of part of the house.
2
State the ruling for partial taking
When only part of the house is taken by the rightful owner, the consideration (the cow) is not returned. The settlement stands.
3
Explain the reasoning
The claimant's unspecified claim could be interpreted as being limited to the remaining portion of the house. Thus, the settlement remains valid for that portion.
4
Identify the exceptional case
If the entire house is taken by the rightful owner, then the consideration must be returned because the claimant's claim is proven entirely false.
This exception shows that the ruling depends on the extent of the taking.
5
Note the underlying principle
The ruling is based on the principle that if the claimant's and defendant's statements can be reconciled, they are reconciled; otherwise, a later judgment may overturn the settlement.

Source Text

Sulh for Claim of Slavery – Validity and Effect
Ruling on sulh for a slavery claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sulh for a slavery claim and explain why it is treated as equivalent to the claimant freeing the slave for payment.

Core Idea
A sulh settling a slavery claim is valid and legally equivalent to the claimant freeing the slave for payment.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in transactions: one person claims that another is his slave. Instead of pursuing the claim in court, they reach a settlement (sulh) where the alleged slave pays the claimant a sum of money to drop the claim. The Hanafi school rules that this sulh is valid, and the claimant's acceptance of money is treated as if he has freed the slave for a price, similar to kitabah. The money is considered compensation for relinquishing the claim of ownership, and the alleged slave becomes free.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is a sulh (settlement) where one man claims another as his slave and receives money from the alleged slave to drop the claim. The ruling is that this sulh is valid (ja'iz).
The ruling is explicitly stated: 'jaza' (it is valid).
2
Determine the Legal Effect
The sulh is in the meaning of freedom (hurriyah) in respect of the claimant. This means that from the claimant's perspective, the transaction is legally equivalent to him freeing the slave for compensation.
The phrase 'fi ma'na al-hurriyah' indicates the legal analogy.
3
Understand the Underlying Analogy
The claimant is treated as if he has freed the slave in exchange for the money received. This is similar to the contract of kitabah where a slave buys his freedom, or to a purchase of freedom. The money is not a sale price for the claimant (since he is not selling a slave he owns), but compensation for relinquishing the claim.
Slavery claims are considered claims of ownership; dropping the claim for payment effectively grants freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ادعى رجل على رجل انه عبده فصالحه على مال بذله له جاز وكان في معنى الحرية في حق المدعي
If a man claims another man as his slave, then he makes sulh with him for money he pays to him, it is valid and is in the meaning of freedom in respect of the claimant.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
The third case: a man claims that another man is his slave. The alleged slave pays the claimant a sum of money to drop the claim of ownership. This sulh is valid. Legally, it is treated as if the claimant has freed the slave for a price (similar to kitabah or purchase of freedom). The money is considered compensation for relinquishing the claim of ownership. From the claimant's perspective, it is as if he is granting freedom to the slave in exchange for payment.

Key Terms
حرية (hurriyah): Freedom from slavery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Sulh in Marriage Dispute: Ruling and Analogy to Khul'
Ruling on sulh in marriage dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sulh when a woman pays a man to drop a marriage claim and explain why it is analogous to khul'.

Core Idea
Sulh to drop a marriage claim is valid and treated like khul'.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a man claims marriage, the woman denies it, but she pays him to drop the case. The Hanafi school validates this transaction, likening it to khul' (divorce with compensation). Understanding this ruling clarifies the interplay between contractual sulh and marital dissolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize the parties: a man claims marriage from a woman who denies it. This is the factual setting of the ruling.
2
Note the sulh arrangement
The woman pays the man a sum of money in exchange for dropping his claim. This is a contractual compromise (sulh) on a disputed right.
3
Recognize the ruling
The text states that the sulh is valid (jā'iz) and is 'in the meaning of khul' (fī ma'nā al-khul').
4
Trace the analogy to khul'
Analyze why the payment is compared to khul': both involve a woman paying to end a marital relationship. Here, the man believes the marriage exists, so the payment secures separation.
5
Apply the broader principle
The commentary adds that sulh on human rights (ḥuqūq al-ʿibād) is permissible, while on divine rights (ḥuqūq Allāh) it is not. This case falls under human rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۷] واذا ادعى رجل على امرأة نكاحا وهى تجحد فصالحته على مال بذلته حتى يترك الدعوى جاز وكان في معنى الخلع

كا اظہار فرمایا۔ اس لئے ثابت ہونے کے بعد اس پر صلح نہیں ہوسکتی۔
اں یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ حقوق انسانی پر صلح ہو سکتی ہے، حقوق اللہ پر صلح نہیں ہو سکتی۔ ۱۴۷۰] (۱۱) ایک آدمی نے ایک عورت پر نکاح کا دعوی کیا اور وہ انکار کرتی ہے۔ پھر عورت نے مرد سے مال پر صلح کی جس کو اس نے خرچ کیا تا کہ مرد دعوی چھوڑ دے تو جائز ہے اور یہ صلح خلع کے حکم میں ہے۔

[17] If a man claims marriage from a woman and she denies, then she settles with him for a payment and gives it so that he drops the claim, it is valid and is in the meaning of khul'. And explanation: This becomes apparent. Therefore, after it is established, sulh upon it is not possible. These issues are upon this principle: sulh on human rights is permissible, on divine rights it is not permissible. [1470] [11] A man claimed marriage from a woman and she denies. Then the woman made a sulh with the man for a payment which he incurred so that the man drops the claim, it is valid and this sulh is in the ruling of khul'. Again: A man claimed from a woman that she was married to him, but the woman denies being married to him. Later, to get rid of him, she gives something and makes sulh with the man so that the man drops the marriage claim, then the woman's giving is valid. For the woman is giving money to get rid of the case. Since it is her wealth, she can spend it to get rid of it. On the woman's side, it will be understood thus: on the man's side, it will be understood that the marriage existed and the woman allegedly gave khul' and gave this money as a means of separation. Therefore, taking this money is permissible for him.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on sulh (compromise) in a disputed marriage claim. The text is a combined Arabic matn and Urdu commentary. The ruling: if a man claims marriage and the woman denies, but she pays him to drop the case, the payment is valid and is treated like khul' (judicial separation with payment). The commentary explains that sulh on human rights (huquq al-ibad) is generally permissible, whereas sulh on divine rights is not. Here, the woman's payment is considered a form of khul' because the man believes the marriage existed and the woman is paying for separation. Hence, it is permissible for him to accept the money.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A contractual compromise to settle a dispute by mutual agreement.
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for a payment to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
