The Invalidity of Sulh When a Woman Claims Marriage and Man Pays to Settle
Ruling on sulh where woman claims marriage and man pays to drop claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a man pays a woman who claims marriage to drop the claim, explain why it is invalid for her to accept, and identify the variant interpretation that treats it as a mahr increase.

Core Idea
A man paying a woman to drop a marriage claim is invalid because the payment lacks a valid legal basis in Hanafi law.

In this passage, we encounter a ruling that may seem counterintuitive: if a woman claims a man married her, and he pays her to drop the claim, the payment is not valid for her to accept. The reasoning explores the woman's possible mental frameworks — neither of which justifies the payment. However, a variant reading opens the door to validity if the payment is interpreted as an increase in mahr. This lesson unpacks the legal logic and the boundaries of sulh in marriage disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the contrasting case
First, clarify the scenario: woman claims marriage, man denies, then pays her to drop the claim. Note that this is the opposite of the previous issue (presumably where the man claims or the woman pays). Understand the legal problem: the man pays, the woman receives — what is the basis?
The 'previous issue' likely involved a different configuration, leading to a different ruling.
2
Analyze the woman's possible justifications
The text presents two possibilities for the woman's perspective: (a) she believes the marriage existed and takes the money for separation, or (b) she believes there was no marriage and simply takes the money. Each leads to a different invalidity.
If she thinks marriage existed, separation payment is like khul', but in khul' the wife pays, not the husband. If she thinks no marriage, taking money without cause is prohibited.
3
Apply the Hanafi concepts of khul' and mahr
Khul' requires the wife to pay the husband for release. Here the husband pays, so khul' is inapplicable. Mahr is a gift from husband to wife upon marriage. Since the marriage is disputed, the payment cannot be mahr unless reinterpreted.
The variant interpretation reinterprets the payment as an increase in mahr, which is permissible.
4
Compare the variant interpretation
One manuscript allows the payment, explaining it as the man giving an increased mahr. This is valid because the woman believes the marriage exists and the man is voluntarily enhancing the mahr, which is allowed. Understand that this variant changes the ruling from batil to sahih.
The variant shows flexibility in legal interpretation while adhering to core principles.
5
State the mufta bihi position and its significance
The preferred view (zahir al-riwayah) is that the payment is invalid. The variant is mentioned but not relied upon. This illustrates how ijtihad resolves conflicts within the school.
Knowing the mufta bihi is essential for fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۷۱ (۱۲) واذا ادعت امرأة نكاحا على رجل فصالحها على مال بذله لها لم يجز

(۱۲) اور اگر دعوی کیا عورت نے نکاح کا مرد پر، پس مرد نے عورت سے صلح کی مال پر جس کو مرد نے عورت کے لئے خرچ کیا تو عورت کے لئے کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس مسئلہ میں مسئلہ نمبرا اسے الٹا ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ عورت نے دعوی کیا کہ میرا اس مرد سے نکاح ہوا ہے۔ اور مرد نے اسکا انکار کیا۔ بعد میں عورت کو مال دے کر صلح کرلی تا کہ جان چھوٹ جائے تو عورت کے لئے مال لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مرد تو سمجھ رہا ہے کہ جان چھڑانے کے لئے رقم دے رہا ہوں۔ اب عورت جو لے رہی ہے وہ کسی اعتبار سے لے رہی ہے۔ اگر یہ سمجھ کر لے رہی ہے کہ نکاح ہوا تھا اور جدا ہونے اور فرقت کے لئے لے رہی ہوں تو جدائیگی کے لئے مرد کی جانب سے کوئی مال نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اگر یہ سمجھ رہی ہے کہ نکاح ہی نہیں ہوا تھا ویسے ہی مال لے رہی ہوں تو ویسے بغیر نکاح کے مال لینا جائز نہیں۔ اس لئے عورت کے لئے یہ مال لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔
ایک نسخے میں ہے کہ عورت کے لئے مال لینا جائز ہے اور اس کی تاویل یہ ہوگی کہ عورت سمجھ رہی ہے کہ نکاح ہوا ہے اور مرد صبح کے طور پر جو مال دے رہا ہے یہ مہر میں زیادتی ہے۔ یعنی مہر ہی گویا کہ زیادہ کر کے دے رہا ہے۔
[1471] [12] And if a woman claims marriage from a man, and he settles with her for a payment and gives it to her, it is not valid. And if a woman claimed marriage from a man, then the man made sulh with the woman for a payment which the man spent for the woman, then taking for the woman is not valid. This issue is the opposite of the previous issue: the woman claimed that she was married to this man, and the man denied it. Later he gave her money and made sulh so that she would drop it, then taking money is not valid for the woman. The man thinks he is giving money to get rid of her. Now the woman is taking it, but from which perspective? If she takes it thinking the marriage existed and she is taking it for separation, then there is no payment from the man for separation. And if she thinks there was no marriage and she is just taking money, then taking money without marriage is not valid. Therefore, taking this money is not valid for the woman. In one copy, it is that taking money is valid for the woman, and its interpretation is that the woman thinks the marriage existed and the man is giving money as an increase in mahr, i.e., he is giving an increased mahr.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage gives the opposite ruling: if a woman claims marriage and the man denies, but he pays her to drop the claim, it is not valid for her to accept the money. The commentary explains the reasoning: the man's perspective is that he is paying to be free, but the woman cannot justify taking it. If she considers the marriage valid and takes it for separation, that would be khul', but in khul' the wife pays, not the husband. If she considers the marriage invalid, then taking money without justification is prohibited. However, one variant allows it, interpreting the payment as an increase in mahr.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): Compromise to end a claim; here it is the man paying the woman to drop her marriage claim.
خلع (khul'): Separation initiated by wife with payment; here it is invoked as a parallel but found inapplicable because the payer is the man.
مهر (mahr): Mandatory gift from husband to wife upon marriage. In the variant, the payment is reinterpreted as an increase in mahr.
تأويل (ta'wil): Interpretation that reconciles a ruling with underlying principles; here, the variant ta'wil transforms an invalid payment into a valid mahr increase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid for the woman to accept payment from the man when she claims marriage and he pays to settle?
A) Because the claim is false.
B) Because the payment cannot be justified as either mahr increase or khul' in this scenario.
C) Because sulh is not allowed in marriage claims.
D) Because only the husband can initiate divorce.

Key Takeaway
A sulh payment from a man to a woman to drop a marriage claim is invalid for the woman to accept, unless reinterpreted as an increase in mahr, but the default ruling is batil.

Sulh on Slavery Claim: Valid Like Manumission
Ruling on sulh in slavery dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sulh in a slavery claim and explain why it is treated as manumission for payment.

Core Idea
A settlement in a slavery dispute where the defendant pays is valid as the slave purchasing his freedom.

The Hanafi school provides a pragmatic approach to resolving disputes through sulh (amicable settlement). In this case, a man claims another is his slave, and the alleged slave pays to settle. The ruling validates this transaction by reinterpreting it as the slave buying his manumission, a known valid contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is a sulh (settlement) in a slavery claim where the defendant pays the claimant. The ruling: it is valid (sahih).
2
Understand the legal construction
From the claimant's perspective, the payment is treated as 'itq ‘ala mal (manumission for payment). The claimant is considered to have freed the slave in exchange for the money.
This is the key legal fiction that makes the transaction valid.
3
Identify the underlying principle
Manumission for payment is a valid contract in Hanafi law. By reinterpreting the sulh as such, the ruling ensures consistency with established principles.
4
Note the practical consequence
The claimant takes the money and the defendant becomes free. The original claim of slavery is effectively dropped without needing proof.
This encourages amicable resolution and avoids litigation.
5
Recognize the broader usul
The underlying principle is that wherever the positions of the parties can be reconciled (by treating the payment as a purchase of freedom), the sulh is upheld. This reflects the Hanafi approach of harmonizing the parties' interests.
As the Urdu commentary states: 'wherever the claimant and the defendant can be reconciled, the matter is accepted.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۷۲ (۱۳) وان ادعى رجل على رجل انه عبده فصالحه على مال اعطاه جازوكان في حق المدعى في معنى العتق على مال

(۱۳) إذا كان دعوى على رجل أنه عبده فصالحه على مال فأعطاه إياه جاز وكان في حق المدعى في معنى العتق على مال (Urdu continuation:) غلام تو یہ مجھ کر دے رہا ہے کہ میں جان چھڑانے کے لئے دے رہا ہوں۔ اور مدعی کے حق میں یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ یہ واقعی اس کا غلام تھا اور مدعی نے صلح کا مال لے کر اس کو آزاد کیا۔ اور مال لے کر آزاد کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے مدعی کا مال لینا جائز ہے۔ اصول پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ جہاں جہاں مدعی اور مدعی علیہ میں جوڑ ہو سکتا ہو تو بات مان لی جائے گی اور جہاں جوڑ نہ ہو سکتا ہو تو الگ فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔
[1472] [13] And if a man claims that another man is his slave, and then settles with him for a payment and gives it to him, it is valid and from the perspective of the claimant it is in the meaning of manumission for payment. If a man claims that another man is his slave, and he settles with him for a payment and gives it to him, it is valid. From the perspective of the claimant it is in the meaning of manumission for payment. (Urdu:) The slave is giving me this, saying 'I am giving to free myself.' And from the claimant's perspective, it will be understood that this really was his slave and the claimant took the sulh money and freed him. And freeing for money is valid. Therefore, the claimant's taking money is valid. The principle has passed earlier that wherever the claimant and the defendant can be reconciled, the matter is accepted; and where reconciliation is not possible, a separate decision is made.

Commentary
This ruling covers a case where a man claims another is his slave, and the alleged slave pays to settle. The payment is valid and is treated as 'itq ‘ala mal (manumission for payment) from the claimant's perspective. The commentary explains that the claimant takes the money and considers the slave freed. This is allowed because manumission for a consideration is valid. The underlying principle is that as long as the positions of the parties can be harmonized (by considering the defendant as a slave who buys his freedom), the settlement is upheld.

Key Terms
عتق على مال ('itq ‘ala mal): Manumission of a slave in exchange for payment; considered a valid contract in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a settlement in a slavery claim by treating the payment as a slave purchasing his freedom through manumission for payment ('itq ‘ala mal).

Sulh on Debt: Not an Exchange but a Partial Waiver
General rule on sulh for debts, with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sulh on a debt is not an exchange, explain why it avoids riba, and derive the ruling from the hadith of Ka'b ibn Malik.

Core Idea
Sulh on debt is partial waiver, not exchange—avoiding riba that would require equality.

When a creditor agrees to accept less than the full debt in settlement, one might think this is a sale of money for money (sarf), which would trigger riba. The Hanafi school clarifies that such a settlement is legally interpreted as the creditor receiving part of his right and forgiving the remainder, thus avoiding any forbidden exchange. This ruling is based on the precedent of the Prophet ﷺ in the hadith of Ka'b ibn Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sulh (settlement) on a debt where the creditor accepts less than the owed amount. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih), not prohibited.
2
Understand the legal recharacterization
The text explains that this sulh is NOT treated as an exchange (mu'awada). Instead, it is treated as the creditor receiving part of his right and dropping the rest. Why? Because if it were an exchange, it would involve riba (as money is being exchanged with a difference in quantity or quality).
The Hanafi school prioritizes avoiding riba over a literal reading of the transaction as a sale.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the hadith of Ka'b ibn Malik. The Prophet ﷺ gestured 'half', and Ka'b took half and left half. This shows that settling for part of a debt is permissible and constitutes dropping the remainder, not exchanging.
The hadith is from Bukhari, classified as ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Example: Creditor has 1000 good dirhams owed. He settles for 500 bad dirhams. We say: he dropped 500 in number and the good quality, and took 500 bad. This is not a sale of 1000 for 500.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۷۳ (۱۴) وكل شيء وقع عليه الصلح وهو مستحق بعقد المداينة لم يحمل على المعاوضة وانما يحمل على انه استوفى بعض حقه واسقط باقيه كمن له على رجل الف

(۱۴) ہر وہ چیز جس پر صلح واقع ہو اور اس میں وہ دین کے عقد سے مستحق ہو تو وہ معاوضہ پر حمل نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ حمل کیا جائے گا اس بات پر کہ بعض حق کو لیا اور باقی کو ساقط کر دیا۔ جیسے کسی کا کسی آدمی پر ہزار درہم عمدہ ہوں، پس اس سے صلح کی پانچ سوکھوٹے پر تو جائز ہے۔ اور ہو گیا گویا کہ اس کو بری کر دیا بعض حق سے۔
عقد مد اینت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ درہم، دینار وغیرہ قرض دیا ہو یا کوئی چیز درہم، دینار کے بدلے بیچی ہو اور وہ مشتری پر قرض ہو۔ اب درہم یا دینار قرض کے بدلے صلح کرنا چاہتا ہے تو اگر عدد کے اعتبار سے یا صفت کے اعتبار سے یامدت کے اعتبار سے کم اور گھٹیا پر صلح کر رہا ہو تو اس کو درہم کے بدلے درہم شار نہیں کریں گے اور معاوضہ نہیں کہیں گے۔ کیونکہ معاوضہ کہیں گے تو برابر سرابر ہونا ضروری ہے ورنہ سود لازم آئے گا جو حرام ہے۔ اس لئے یوں تاویل کریں گے کہ مدعی نے کچھ حق لیا اور کچھ ساقط کر دیا۔ مثلا کسی آدمی کا کسی آدمی پر ایک ہزار عمدہ در ہم قرض تھے۔ اس نے پانچ سو گھٹیا اور کھوٹا درہم پر صلح کی تو یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ عدد کے اعتبار سے باقی پانچ سو چھوڑ دیا اور صفت کے اعتبار سے عمدہ کو ساقط کر کے گھٹیالیا۔ یوں نہیں کہیں گے کہ ایک ہزار درہم کے بدلے پانچ سو درہم لیا۔ اگر ایسا کہیں تو سود لازم آئے گا جو حرام ہے۔ عدد کے اعتبار سے قرض ساقط کرنے کا ثبوت یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن كعب ابن مالک انه كان له على عبد الله بن ابی حدرد الاسلمي مال فلقيه فلزمه حتى ارتفعت اصواتها فمر بهما النبي الا الله فقال يا كعب فاشار بيده كانه يقول النصف فاخذ نصف مـالـه عـلـيـه وترك نصفا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب هل يشير الامام با صلح ص ۲۷۳ نمبر ۲۷۰۶) اس حدیث میں حضرت کعب نے حضور کے کہنے پر آدھے دین پر صلح کر لی۔ اور حدیث میں ترک نصفا سے معلوم ہوا کہ آدھا چھوڑ دیا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) کعب بن مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کا عبد اللہ بن حدرد پر کچھ مال تھا، پس حضرت کعب نے ان سے ملاقات کی اور اس کے پیچھے لگ گئے ۔ یہاں تک کہ دونوں کی آواز بلند ہوگئی ۔ پس وہاں سے حضور گزرے اور کہا اے کعب ! اور ہاتھ سے اشارہ کیا۔ گویا کہ فرمارہے ہیں کہ آدھا قرض لے لو۔ پس اس پر کا آدھا مال لیا اور آدھا چھوڑ دیا۔
[1473] [14] And everything that sulh occurs upon, and it is owed by a debt contract, it is not treated as an exchange, but rather it is treated as that he has received some of his right and dropped the rest. For example, someone has a thousand dirhams owed to him, then he settles for five hundred bad dirhams, it is valid and he becomes as if he has waived part of the right. The meaning of 'aqd al-mudayana' is that dirhams, dinars, etc. are loaned or an item is sold for dirhams/dinars and is owed. When one wants to settle a loan of dirhams or dinars for less in number or inferior in quality or lesser in term, it is not considered a sale (sarf) and not called an exchange. Because if it were an exchange, it would require equality otherwise riba would occur, which is prohibited. Therefore, we interpret it as the creditor received part of his right and dropped the rest. For example, someone had a loan of 1000 good dirhams, and he settled for 500 bad dirhams, it is understood that he dropped 500 in number and dropped the good quality and took inferior. It is not said that he took 500 dirhams in exchange for 1000 dirhams; if so, riba would occur. Proof of dropping part of the debt is this hadith: From Ka'b ibn Malik that he had some money owed by 'Abdullah ibn Abi Hadrad al-Aslami. He met him and cornered him until their voices rose. The Prophet ﷺ passed by and said, 'O Ka'b!' and gestured with his hand as if saying 'half.' So he took half of what was owed to him and left half. (Bukhari, chapter on whether the imam suggests sulh, p. 273, no. 2706). In this hadith, Ka'b made sulh for half of the debt at the Prophet's suggestion, and the phrase 'left half' indicates that he dropped half.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage provides a fundamental rule about sulh in debts: when a sulh is made concerning a right owed by a debt contract, it is not treated as a sale or exchange (mu'awada) to avoid riba. Instead, it is treated as the creditor receiving part of his due and forgiving the rest. The commentary elaborates that if it were considered an exchange, riba would arise because the quantity or quality differs; so we interpret it as a partial waiver. The hadith of Ka'b ibn Malik serves as proof: the Prophet indicated settling for half, and Ka'b took half and left half, which is a precedent for dropping part of a debt via sulh.

Key Terms
معاوضة (mu'awada): An exchange contract such as sale; here contrasted with sulh, which is not a true exchange to avoid riba.
عقد المداينة ('aqd al-mudayana): A debt contract, typically a loan or credit sale where payment is deferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is sulh on a debt for less than owed not considered a sale (mu'awada)?
A) Because the parties do not intend a sale.
B) Because it would require equality and cause riba otherwise.
C) Because debt cannot be sold.
D) Because the creditor must forgive the entire debt.

Key Takeaway
Sulh on a debt for less than owed is valid because it is legally treated as the creditor receiving part of his right and dropping the rest, not as an exchange that would involve riba.

Appointing an Agent for Sulh and Agent's Liability
Proof from hadith and ruling on agent's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on appointing an agent for sulh and explain when the agent becomes personally liable.

Core Idea
An agent in a sulh of exchange becomes personally liable even without explicit guarantee.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on appointing an agent for sulh (compromise). The source establishes that such agency is permissible, supported by the Prophet's approval of the Hasan-Mu'awiyah reconciliation. Crucially, when the sulh is of the exchange type (mu'awadah), the agent becomes a guarantor (dhamin) even if not explicitly stipulated, because it resembles a sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: appointing an agent for sulh. The ruling is ja'iz (permissible) based on the hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof: the hadith of Mu'awiyah sending two agents to Hasan ibn Ali, and the Prophet's glad tidings. This establishes the permissibility.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves permissibility: the Prophet praised the reconciliation, implying the actions of the agents were valid. Thus, agency in sulh is sanctioned.
The Prophet's approval indicates legal validity.
4
Note the classification of sulh
Distinguish between sulh of isqat (dropping) and mu'awadah (exchange). In exchange-type, the agent automatically becomes dhamin because it is akin to a sale.
Hanafi classification: mu'awadah sulh transfers liability to agent.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the agent makes a mu'awadah sulh, he is personally liable for the payment, not the principal, unless he explicitly guaranteed otherwise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلح
الوكيل ما صالحه عليه الا ان يضمنه والمال لازم للموكل [۱۹] (۲۰) 
صلح کی دوسری قسم وہ ہے جس میں اسقاط نہیں ہوتا ہے بلکہ بدل اور معاوضہ کی شکل ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے اقرار کے بعد مال کے بدلے مال پر صلح کرے تو اس صلح میں وکیل ذمہ دار ہوتا ہے۔
یہ بیچ کی شکل ہو جاتی ہے اور بیچ میں خود وکیل ذمہ دار ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس صلح میں وکیل ضامن نہ بھی ہو پھر بھی صلح کرنے کی وجہ سے وکیل ضامن ہو جائے گا۔ صلح میں وکیل بنانے کا ثبوت اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت معاویہ نے عبدالرحمن بن سمرہ اور عبد اللہ بن عامر بن کریز کو صلح کا وکیل بنا کر حضرت حسن بن علی کے پاس بھیجا۔ اور انہوں نے تمام ذمہ داری لی جس کی وجہ سے حضرت حسن اور حضرت معاویہ کے درمیان صلح ہوئی جس کے بارے میں حضور نے ممبر پر خوشخبری دی تھی کہ میرا یہ بیٹا دو بڑی جماعت کے درمیان صلح کرائے گا۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ فال سمعت الحسن يقول استقبل والله الحسن بن على معاوية بكتائب امثال الجبال ... فبعث اليه رجلين من قريش من بنی عبد شمس عبد الرحمن بن سمرة و عبد الله بن عامر بن كريز فقال (معاوية) اذهبا الى هذا الرجل فاعرضا عليه وقولا له واطلبا اليه فاتياه فدخلا عليه فتكلما (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب قول النبي محسن بن على ان ابني هذا اسيد ولعل اللہ ان تصلح به بین فکتین بھیجا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ صلح کے لئے وکیل بنا سکتے ہیں۔ [۱۴۷۹]
Chapter of Sulh. The agent: whatever he settles upon, unless he guarantees it, the payment is binding on the principal. The second type of sulh is that which does not involve dropping (of rights) but rather takes the form of exchange and compensation. For example, sulh for property in exchange for property after an admission, then in this sulh the agent is liable. This becomes a form of sale, and in sale the agent himself is liable. Therefore, even if he does not guarantee in this sulh, due to making the sulh he becomes a guarantor. The proof for appointing an agent in sulh is in this hadith: Mu'awiyah sent 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Samurah and 'Abdullah ibn 'Amir ibn Kurayz as agents for sulh to Hasan ibn 'Ali. They took full responsibility, resulting in peace between Hasan and Mu'awiyah, about which the Prophet gave glad tidings on the pulpit: 'This son of mine will reconcile two great groups.' A piece of the hadith: 'I heard al-Hasan say: By Allah, al-Hasan ibn 'Ali met Mu'awiyah with battalions like mountains... then he sent to him two men from Quraysh from Banu 'Abd Shams: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Samurah and 'Abdullah ibn 'Amir ibn Kurayz. Mu'awiyah said: Go to this man, present it to him, speak to him, and request him. So they went, entered upon him, and spoke.' (Bukhari, Chapter of the Prophet's saying: 'My son is a sayyid, perhaps Allah will reconcile through him two great groups.') So it is learned that one can appoint an agent for sulh.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on sulh (compromise/settlement) by establishing the permissibility of appointing an agent (wakil) for sulh. The Arabic matn states a default rule: if an agent makes a sulh, the payment is binding on the principal (the one who appointed him) unless the agent himself guarantees the payment. The Urdu commentary then explains that this type of sulh is one of exchange (mu'awadah), not of dropping rights (isqat). Because it resembles a sale, the agent becomes personally liable (dhamin) even without explicit stipulation. The proof for agency in sulh is the historical event of the peace treaty between Hasan and Mu'awiyah, where Mu'awiyah appointed two men as his agents. The Prophet's hadith praising this reconciliation is cited (from Bukhari), establishing the legal precedent that one may delegate another to conduct a sulh. The passage sets the foundation: sulh by an agent is valid, and in cases of exchange, the agent bears liability.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by a principal (muwakkil) to conduct a sulh on his behalf.
صلح (sulh): A contract of compromise, either by dropping a claim (isqat) or by exchange (mu'awadah).
ضامن (dhamin): A guarantor or one who is personally liable for payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when an agent makes a sulh of the exchange type without the principal's permission and does not guarantee the payment?
A) The sulh is void.
B) The principal is bound by the payment.
C) The agent is personally liable for the payment.
D) The sulh is suspended pending principal's approval.

Key Takeaway
Appointing an agent for sulh is permissible; in exchange-type sulh, the agent automatically becomes personally liable.

The Four Forms of Sulh by an Unauthorized Person (Fuduli)
Classification of sulh by an unauthorized person into four cases based on assumption of liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four forms of sulh made by an unauthorized person (fuduli) based on whether he assumes personal liability, and state the resulting ruling for each form.

Core Idea
A fuduli's sulh is binding without permission if he guarantees payment or delivers his own property.

This lesson classifies the situation where someone makes a sulh (compromise settlement) on behalf of another without prior authorization. The key factor determining whether the sulh is immediately binding or suspended is whether the unauthorized person (fuduli) assumes personal liability for the payment. Understanding these four forms is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi rules of agency and guarantee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fuduli's action
The fuduli makes a sulh agreement with a claimant on behalf of a principal (the defendant) without prior permission.
All four forms share this starting point.
2
Determine if the fuduli assumes liability
Look for three indicators: (1) he explicitly guarantees (daman) the payment, (2) he specifies the property as his own (e.g., 'my slave'), or (3) he actually hands over the sulh amount.
If any of these is present, the fuduli has assumed personal liability.
3
Ruling when liability is assumed
If the fuduli assumes liability, the sulh is immediately binding (tamma al-sulh) without needing the principal's permission. The fuduli must deliver the property or pay the amount.
This covers forms 1, 2, and 3.
4
Ruling when no liability is assumed
If the fuduli does not guarantee, specify his own property, or deliver the amount, the sulh is suspended (mawquf). It becomes binding only if the principal ratifies it; otherwise it becomes void (batil).
This is the fourth form.

(20) If he made a sulh on his behalf for something without his permission, then it is of four types: (1) If he made sulh for property and became its guarantor, the sulh is complete. (2) Similarly, if he said 'I have made sulh with you for this one thousand of mine' or 'for this slave of mine,' the sulh is complete, and the delivery of that property to him is binding. (3) Similarly, if he said 'I have made sulh with you for one thousand' and handed it over. He makes sulh as a fuduli (unauthorized person). If he took responsibility for the sulh property or handed over his own property to the claimant, then the sulh becomes complete without the permission of the defendant. And if the fuduli did not take responsibility for paying the property nor gave his own property, the sulh is suspended pending the principal's permission. If he permits, the sulh becomes complete; if not, it becomes void. When the fuduli assumes liability, the matter of paying the money is not on the principal, so the sulh is complete without his permission. Because the fuduli made the sulh and also paid the money. He said: 'I have made sulh with you for this one thousand of mine' or 'for this slave of mine' – the sulh is complete and delivery to him is binding. Likewise if he said 'I have made sulh with you for one thousand' and handed it over. And if he said 'I have made sulh with you for one thousand' and did not hand it over, the contract is suspended. If the defendant permits, it becomes valid and the one thousand becomes binding on him; if he does not permit, it becomes void. The author mentioned three ways in which the fuduli takes responsibility: (1) The fuduli made sulh for property and took responsibility for handing over the property. (2) He said 'I make sulh with you for this one thousand of mine' or 'for this slave of mine' – so he made sulh for his own slave, thus he took responsibility for giving the slave or one thousand, so it is no longer suspended upon the principal's permission. (3) The third form: he did not name his slave or his thousand but made a sulh for an absolute thousand and gave the thousand from his side, so the fuduli's responsibility occurred, thus the sulh is complete.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage details the four possible scenarios when an unauthorized person (fuduli) makes a sulh on behalf of someone else (the principal/defendant) without permission. The classification hinges on whether the fuduli assumes personal liability for the payment (dhaman) or not. 

**First form:** The fuduli makes sulh for a property and explicitly guarantees (yadman) it. The sulh is immediately binding (tamma al-sulh) because the fuduli's own liability substitutes for the principal's. 

**Second form:** The fuduli says 'I have made sulh with you for this one thousand of mine' or 'this slave of mine.' By specifying his own asset, he effectively takes responsibility; the sulh is binding and he must deliver the asset. 

**Third form:** The fuduli says 'I make sulh for one thousand' (without specifying his own) and actually hands over the money (sallamaha ilayh). Since he has physically paid, the sulh is binding regardless of the principal's permission. 

**Fourth form:** The fuduli says 'I make sulh for one thousand' but does not hand it over (lam yusallimha). The contract becomes suspended (mawquf): it depends on the defendant's (i.e., the original debtor or principal) ratification. If he permits, the sulh is valid and the thousand becomes binding on him; if he refuses, it is void. 

The commentary emphasizes that the key distinction is whether the fuduli has made himself liable for the payment (either by guarantee, by specifying his own property, or by actual delivery). If not, the sulh remains in abeyance. This protects the principal from being bound without his consent.

Key Terms
فضولي (fuduli): An unauthorized person who acts on behalf of another without prior permission.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee of payment; the fuduli takes personal responsibility for the sulh amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A fuduli says to a claimant, 'I make sulh with you for my slave, Zayd,' and then hands over the slave. The principal has not given permission. What is the ruling?
A) The sulh is suspended pending the principal's permission.
B) The sulh is void because the principal did not authorize.
C) The sulh is immediately binding because the fuduli specified his own property and delivered it.
D) The sulh is binding only on the fuduli to deliver the slave, but the principal can reclaim it.

Key Takeaway
A fuduli's sulh is immediately binding when he assumes personal liability (through guarantee, specifying own property, or actual delivery); otherwise it is suspended.

Sulh by One Partner: Options for the Other
Ruling on options after partial settlement of joint debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to a creditor when his joint creditor settles his share of a joint debt, and identify the condition that modifies the second option.

Core Idea
One partner's settlement does not extinguish the other's right; he may claim directly or share the goods.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in financial transactions where two parties are joint creditors. When one creditor compromises his share for goods, what happens to the other's claim? The Hanafi ruling provides clear options that protect the non-settling creditor's rights, while also allowing a conditional alternative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the settlement
Recognize that there are two joint creditors (e.g., Zayd and Umar) and one debtor (Khalid). One creditor (Zayd) settles his share (500 of 1000) by accepting a cloth from the debtor.
The settlement is a sulh, valid in Hanafi law.
2
Understand the first option
The non-settling partner (Umar) may directly pursue the debtor (Khalid) for his own half of the original debt (500). This is because the settlement only affects the settling partner's share.
Umar's right against Khalid remains intact.
3
Understand the second option
Alternatively, Umar may take half of the cloth that Zayd accepted. This option is available only if Zayd has not become a guarantor (damin) for the debt.
If Zayd becomes a guarantor, Umar must claim from Zayd, not the cloth.
4
Apply the exception
The text mentions 'unless his partner becomes the guarantor of that day' – meaning if Zayd guarantees Umar's share, Umar cannot take the cloth but must claim from Zayd.
The exact wording is unclear, but the gist is a conditional modification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۸۱) (۲۲) اگر دین دو شریکوں کے درمیان ہو پس ان میں سے ایک نے اپنے حصے کے بدلے میں صلح کر لی کپڑے پر تو اس کے شریک کو اختیار ہے، اگر چاہے تو اس کا پیچھا کرے جس پر دین ہے اپنے آدھے دین کے لئے اور اگر چاہے تو آدھا کپڑا لے لے ، مگر یہ کہ اس کا شریک جو تھائی دن کا ضامن ہو جائے۔ اس مسئلے میں تین صورتیں ہیں جن کو ایک ساتھ بیان کر دیا ہے۔ مثلا زید اور عمر کا ایک ہزار دین خالد پر تھا، زید نے اپنے حصے پانچ سو کے بدلے میں صلح کر کے کپڑا لے لیا۔ اب عمر شریک کو دو اختیار ہیں۔ یا تو اپنا حصہ ( پانچ سو درہم) براہ راست خالد سے وصول کرے اور اس کا پیچھا کرے۔ کیونکہ عمر کا قرض اصل میں خالد پر ہے جس نے کپڑا دیا ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ اور دوسرا اختیار یہ ہے کہ اس کا جو
(1381) (22) If there is a debt between two partners, and one of them makes a sulh for his share on a cloth, then his partner has a choice: if he wishes, he may pursue the one who owes the debt for his half of the debt, and if he wishes, he may take half of the cloth, unless his partner becomes the guarantor of that day (?) This issue has three scenarios which have been mentioned together. For example, Zayd and 'Umar had a thousand owed by Khalid. Zayd made sulh for his share of five hundred and took a cloth. Now 'Umar, the partner, has two options: either to recover his share (five hundred dirhams) directly from Khalid and pursue him. Because 'Umar's debt is originally upon Khalid who gave the cloth, so he can recover from him. The second option is that his (the partner's)...

Commentary
This passage deals with a joint debt owned by two partners (sharikan) against a single debtor (e.g., Zayd and 'Umar have a joint claim of 1000 against Khalid). One partner (Zayd) settles his half (500) by accepting a piece of cloth from the debtor in lieu of his share. The question: what are the rights of the other partner ('Umar)? 

The text gives 'Umar two options: (1) He may pursue the debtor (Khalid) directly for his own half (500) because the original debt is still due to him; or (2) He may take half of the cloth that Zayd accepted, i.e., share in the settlement. However, this second option is conditional: unless Zayd becomes the guarantor (damin) of that—meaning if Zayd guarantees to pay 'Umar's share, then 'Umar must accept from Zayd. The passage mentions three scenarios (thawaan) but the text cuts off before detailing them. The example clarifies: Zayd's settlement does not extinguish 'Umar's right against Khalid; 'Umar can still claim his half. Alternatively, he can choose to take part of the cloth, effectively approving Zayd's settlement as part of the joint claim.

Key Terms
شريك (shareek): A partner in a joint debt; each has an undivided share in the claim.
صلح (sulh): Compromise; here, one partner settles his share by accepting goods instead of cash.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When one of two joint creditors settles his share by accepting a cloth from the debtor, what options does the other creditor have?
A) He can only take his share from the debtor.
B) He can only take half of the cloth.
C) He can either pursue the debtor for his share or take half of the cloth.
D) He must accept the settlement and has no further claim.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when one joint creditor settles his share, the other retains a choice: claim directly from the debtor or share the settlement goods, unless the settling partner becomes a guarantor.

Settlement with Excess Over Share: Avoiding Riba
States condition for settlement validity when amount exceeds share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a valid settlement when a co-heir takes more than his share of a particular genus, and apply the Hanafi principle of equality in same-genus transactions to determine validity.

Core Idea
Excess over share in same-genus items must be offset by other assets to avoid riba.

In inheritance settlements, heirs may agree that one heir takes more than his entitled share of a specific asset, such as gold. However, Islamic law prohibits riba (interest) in exchanges of same-genus items. This lesson explains how the Hanafi school validates such settlements by requiring that the excess be compensated with assets of a different genus, ensuring equality in the same-genus portion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a settlement (sulh) where a co-heir receives more than his share of a particular genus (e.g., gold). The ruling is that such a settlement is valid (sahih) if the excess is compensated by other assets from the estate.
The validity hinges on the condition that the same-genus part remains equal.
2
Recognize the condition for validity
The key condition is that the excess over the heir's share must be matched by other assets from the estate (e.g., silver, cows) that are of a different genus. This ensures that the portion of the same-genus asset taken is exactly equal to the heir's share.
If the excess is not compensated, the settlement becomes invalid due to riba.
3
Apply the principle of same-genus exchange
The underlying principle is that for same-genus items (e.g., gold for gold, silver for silver), equality in quantity and immediate possession (qabd fi al-majlis) are required to avoid riba. Here, the heir's share of gold is equal to what he receives in gold, and the extra gold is offset by different assets.
This principle is derived from the general prohibition of riba al-fadl.
4
Examine the example given
The text provides an example: if settlement is for a dinar (gold coin), the heir must receive more than one dinar from the estate; his share equals one dinar, and the excess is compensated by five hundred dirhams and cows. If he receives less than a dinar, the settlement is invalid because the gold portion would be unequal.
The example illustrates how the condition works in practice.
5
Conclude the ruling
Thus, the settlement is valid only when the same-genus portion is exactly equal to the heir's share and the excess is covered by other assets. This avoids riba and ensures fairness.
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah and is agreed upon within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثانى ۳۳۷ كتاب الصلح يكون ما اعطوه اكثر من نصيبه من ذلك الجنس حتى يكون نصيبه بمثله والزيادة بحقه من بقية الميراث پانچ گایوں کے مقابلے میں ہو جائیں۔ اور دینار پرصلح کرنا ہوتو ہیں دینار سے زیادہ ہونا چاہئے۔ تا کہ اس کوجو وراثت میں سے ہیں دینار ملنے والے ہیں اس کے برابر ہیں دینار ہو جائے اور جو زیادہ ہو وہ پانچ سو درہم اور گایوں کے مقابلے میں ہو جائے۔ میں دینار سے کم پر صلح جائز نہیں تا کہ پانچ سو چاندی پانچ سو چاندی کے برابر ہو جائے ، اور ہمیں دینار میں دینار کے برابر ہو جائے ۔ اور ایک جنس ہونے کی وجہ سے سود لازم نہ آئے۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ ایک جنس ہو تو برابری ضروری ہے تا کہ سود لازم نہ ہو۔ اس لئے اس کے حصے سے زیادہ پر صلح کرنا ضروری جتنا سونا سونے کے بدلے میں یا چاندی چاندی کے بدلے میں ہو اس پر مجلس میں قبضہ کرنا بھی ضروری ہے تا کہ سود لازم نہ آئے۔
The [settlement] is when they give him more than his share from that genus, so that his share is equal to it, and the excess is due from the rest of the inheritance. In the case of five cows compared, and if settlement is made on a dinar, then it should be more than a dinar, so that what he receives from inheritance equals a dinar, and the excess is against five hundred dirhams and the cows. Settlement for less than a dinar is not valid, so that five hundred silver is equal to five hundred silver, and we have a dinar equal to a dinar, and due to the same genus, riba does not apply. The principle: this issue is based on the principle that if it is the same genus, equality is necessary so that riba does not apply. Therefore, settlement for more than his share is necessary, and as much gold for gold or silver for silver, possession in the sitting is also necessary so that riba does not apply.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from the book of Sulh (settlement) explains the condition for a valid settlement when a co-heir takes more than his share of a particular asset (e.g., gold) from the estate. The ruling states that it is permissible if the excess is compensated by other assets (e.g., silver, cows) from the remaining inheritance. The key principle is that when exchanging same genus items (gold for gold, silver for silver), equality and immediate possession are required to avoid riba (interest). Thus, if a brother takes more gold than his entitled share, the excess must be balanced by other property so that the gold portion remains equal, and the extra is against other assets. This follows the Hanafi rule of maintaining equality in same-genus transactions.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): Settlement or compromise between parties, often to avoid litigation.
نصيب (nasib): Share or portion of inheritance allocated to an heir.
جنس (jins): Genus or category of items, especially regarding riba (e.g., gold, silver).
ربا (riba): Interest or usury, prohibited in transactions of same genus items if not equal or deferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To ensure the settlement is final and binding
B) Because gold and silver are of the same genus, and equality is required to avoid riba
C) Because the other heirs must approve the settlement
D) Because the excess is considered a gift and must be reciprocated

Key Takeaway
A settlement where a co-heir takes more than his share of a same-genus asset is valid only if the excess is compensated by other assets of a different genus, thereby avoiding riba.

Ruling on Including Debt in Settlement (Sulh)
Explains invalidity and validity of settlement when debt is included

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid forms of including a debt in a settlement contract, and apply the Hanafi principle that a debt can only be owned by the debtor through forgiveness.

Core Idea
A debt cannot be transferred to a non-debtor; only forgiveness to the debtor is valid in settlement.

This passage from the book of Sulh clarifies two contrasting scenarios when a third-party debt is included in a settlement between heirs. The key distinction lies in who becomes the owner of the debt: if the debt is assigned to non-debtors, the settlement is invalid; if the debtors are released (forgiven), it is valid. Understanding this rule prevents common errors in inheritance settlements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage and note the two distinct rulings: invalid (29) and valid (30) regarding inclusion of debt in sulh.
The invalidity/validity hinges on whether the debt is transferred to non-debtors or the debtors are released.
2
Analyze the invalid case (29)
Determine why the settlement is batil. The key principle: a debt can only be owned by the debtor. Assigning it to other heirs is tantamount to transferring ownership to non-debtors, which is impermissible.
The example of Zaid's sons: one heir cannot 'sell' his share of the debt to his brothers.
3
Analyze the valid case (30)
Understand that when the settling heir stipulates forgiveness of his share of the debt, the settlement becomes valid. This is because the debtor is made the owner (i.e., forgiven).
The hadith of Hasan ibn Ali and the Prophet's instruction support this permissibility.
4
Examine the dalil
Locate the hadith cited from Bukhari. The Prophet's command to forgive debts indicates the validity of ibra' (release). This serves as the evidence for the valid case.
The hadith shows that forgiving a debt is a praiseworthy act, not that transfer of debt is allowed.
5
Note the hila (stratagem)
Review the practical stratagem described in the commentary: the remaining heirs lend money to the debtor, who then pays the exiting heir, who returns the money to the others. This effectively allows collection without transferring the debt.
This hila avoids the prohibition while achieving the desired outcome.

(29) And if in the estate there is a debt owed by people, and they include it in the settlement on condition that they release the settler from it and the debt remains for them, then the settlement is invalid. ... It is necessary to understand a principle: the owner of a debt can only make the debtor the owner, meaning forgive the debt; he cannot make someone else the owner. Example: Zaid dies leaving five sons and a debt of 500 dirhams from Khalid. One son, 'Umar, wants to exit the inheritance and settle for some money, and wants to assign the debt to his brothers. The ruling is that taking something for the debt and making the brothers owners is invalid. (30) If they stipulate that they release the debtors from it and they do not return upon them with the share of the settler, then the settlement is valid. Explanation: the exiting heir says he forgives his share of the debt, and the remaining heirs will not collect it. This is valid because they made the debtor the owner (forgave). A hadith: Hasan ibn 'Ali gifted his debt to a man, and the Prophet said: 'Whoever has a right against someone, let him give it or seek release.' And Jabir said: 'My father was killed and he had a debt. The Prophet asked the creditors to accept the fruits of my garden and release my father.' (Bukhari). The principle: making the debtor own the debt (forgiveness) is valid. A stratagem: the remaining heirs lend the debtor money, he pays the exiting heir, and that heir returns it to them, so the debt is effectively collected.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from the book of Sulh (settlement) addresses the ruling on including a debt owed by third parties in a settlement between heirs. The first case (29) declares invalid any settlement where the withdrawing heir (musalih) is released from his share of the debt, but the other heirs retain the right to collect it. The reason is that a debt cannot be transferred to a non-debtor; ownership of a debt can only be given to the debtor himself, i.e., through forgiveness (ibra'). The example clarifies: if one heir wants to exit and have his brothers collect his share of a debt from a third party, this is invalid because the debt is not a tangible asset that can be owned by others. The second case (30) states that if the stipulation is that the debtors are released from the settler's share (i.e., forgiven), then the settlement is valid. This is supported by a hadith from Bukhari where the Prophet encouraged forgiving debts. The commentary also provides a legal stratagem (hila): the remaining heirs can lend money to the debtor, who then pays the exiting heir, and the exiting heir returns the money to the others, thereby transferring the debt effectively.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): Debt owed by a third party, considered a right (haqq) in the estate.
إبراء (ibra'): Release or forgiveness of a debt, making the debtor the owner of the debt (i.e., absolving him).
غرماء (ghurama'): In this context, debtors (those who owe money), though literally 'creditors' in other contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the settler must receive his full share in cash
B) Because a debt cannot be owned by anyone other than the debtor himself
C) Because the debtors did not consent to the settlement
D) Because the remaining heirs did not agree

Key Takeaway
Including debt in settlement is only valid if the debtor is released from the debt, not if the debt is transferred to another non-debtor.

Compromise on Debt with Heirs: Conditions and Ruling
Ruling with proof on sulh involving heirs and debtors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a compromise (ṣulḥ) between heirs and creditors is valid, explain the underlying principle of making the debtor owner of the debt, and apply the legal device (ḥīla) for remaining heirs to recover their shares.

Core Idea
A compromise on debt is valid when the debtor is made the owner of the debt through forgiveness.

This lesson examines a Hanafi ruling from the Book of Compromise (Kitāb al-Ṣulḥ) concerning a scenario where heirs and creditors agree to settle a debt owed to the estate. The passage presents the conditions for validity, the proof from a ḥadīth, and a legal device (ḥīla) for the remaining heirs to recover their shares. Understanding this ruling clarifies how Hanafī fiqh handles debt forgiveness and conditional compromises in inheritance disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the key condition
The passage involves heirs (including one who exits via takhāruj), creditors, and a debtor. The condition stipulated is that the creditors are absolved of the debt and the compromising heir does not have recourse against them for his share.
The compromising heir forgives his share, and the remaining heirs also agree not to collect that share.
2
State the ruling and its basis
The compromise is valid (jāʾiz). The basis is that the debtor is made the owner of the debt, i.e., the debt is forgiven, which is permissible.
The ḥanafī principle: making the debtor owner of his own debt is equivalent to forgiveness.
3
Analyze the proof (dalīl)
The passage cites an athar from Ḥasan bin ʿAlī gifting his debt and a ḥadīth where the Prophet (ﷺ) allowed creditors to accept fruit in lieu of debt and forgive the deceased. This demonstrates the permissibility of forgiving a debt in exchange for property.
The ḥadīth is from Ṣaḥīḥ al-Bukhārī, showing that forgiving debt is a valid form of compromise.
4
Understand the legal device (ḥīla)
If the remaining heirs wish to recover their shares, they can use a ḥīla: the remaining heirs give a new loan to the debtor, the debtor gives that amount to the exiting heir, and the exiting heir returns it to the remaining heirs. This makes the debt directly owed to the remaining heirs.
This ḥīla ensures that the compromise does not disadvantage the remaining heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلح
شرطوا ان يبرئ الغرماء منه ولا يرجع عليهم بنصيب المصالح عنه فالصلح جائز . تشریح نکلنے والے اور تخارج کرنے والے وارث نے یوں کہا کہ دین میں سے جو میرا حصہ ہوگا میں اس کو قرض والوں سے معاف کرتا ہوں ۔
صلى الله
میر اوہ حصہ باقی ورثہ بھی قرضداروں سے وصول نہیں کریں گے۔ اس شرط پر جو جائداد حاضر ہے اس کے بدلے میں صلح کیا تو جائز ہے۔ یہاں جس پر قرض تھا اس کو قرض کا مالک بنایا یعنی معاف کیا اس لئے یہ جائز ہو گیا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ وهـب الحسن بن علي عليهما السلام دینه لرجل وقال النبى الله من كان له عليه حق فليعطه او ليتحلله منه وقال جابر قتل ابی و علیه دین فسأل النبي غرماء ٥ ان يقبلو ثمر حائطى ويحللوا ابی بخاری شریف ، باب از او هب دینا علی رجل ص ۳۵۴ نمبر ۲۶۰۱) اس حدیث میں دین معاف کرنے کا تذکرہ ہے جو جائز ہے۔
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ جس پر دین تھا اسی کو دین کا مالک بنادیا یعنی معاف کر دیا تو جائز ہوگا۔ اس کا حیلہ یہ ہے کہ باقی ورثہ قرضدار کو دوبارہ قرض دے اور وہ رقم قرضدار تخارج کرنے والے وارث کو دے اور تخارج کرنے والے
وارث وہ رقم پھر باقی ورثہ کو دے دے تو اب چونکہ باقی ورثہ کا قرض براہ راست قرض والوں پر ہو گیا اس لئے وہ وصول کر سکتے ہیں۔
Book of Compromise. They stipulated that the creditors be absolved of it and that he does not have recourse against them for the share of the one compromising with him, so the compromise is valid. The explaining and exiting heir said: 'From the debt, whatever my share is, I forgive it to the creditors.' ... The remaining heirs also will not collect that share from the creditors. On this condition, in exchange for the present property, a compromise was made, so it is valid. Here, the one who owed the debt was made the owner of the debt, i.e., forgiven, therefore it became valid. There is an athar: Hasan bin Ali (peace be upon them both) gifted his debt to a man, and the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Whoever has a right due to him, let him give it or let him seek release from it.' Jabir said: 'My father was killed and he had a debt, so the Prophet asked the creditors to accept the fruit of my garden and forgive my father.' (Bukhari Sharif, Chapter on gifting a debt to a man, p. 354, no. 2601). This hadith mentions forgiving a debt, which is valid. The principle: this issue is based on the principle that whoever owed the debt was made the owner of the debt, i.e., forgiven, so it is valid. The legal device is that the remaining heirs give a new loan to the debtor, and the debtor gives that amount to the exiting heir, and the exiting heir then gives that amount to the remaining heirs. Now, since the remaining heirs' debt becomes directly upon the debtor, they can collect it.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Book of Compromise (Kitab al-Sulh) concerning a specific scenario involving heirs, a debtor, and creditors. The ruling states that if heirs stipulate that they absolve the creditors and do not seek recourse against them for the share of the heir who is making a compromise (sulh), then the compromise is valid. The commentary explains that the heir who is exiting (takhāruj) says he forgives his share of the debt to the creditors, and the remaining heirs also agree not to collect that share, in exchange for some present property. This is valid because the debtor is made the owner of the debt (i.e., the debt is forgiven to him). The proof (dalil) is an athar (narrated effect) from Hasan bin Ali and a hadith from Jabir where the Prophet (ﷺ) allowed creditors to accept fruit in lieu of debt and forgive the deceased. The passage then provides a legal device (hila) for the remaining heirs to recover their shares: they give a new loan to the debtor, the debtor gives that amount to the exiting heir, and the exiting heir gives it back to the remaining heirs, thus making the debt directly owed to them.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A contract to settle a dispute by mutual agreement, often involving a compromise on a claim.
تخارج (takhāruj): An arrangement where one or more heirs exit from the estate in exchange for consideration, often used in debt scenarios.
دين (dayn): A debt or financial obligation owed to another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, under what condition is a compromise (sulh) between heirs and creditors valid?
A) The heirs must forgive the entire debt unconditionally.
B) The stipulation that the creditors are absolved and the compromising heir does not recourse against them.
C) The debtor must pay the full amount immediately.
D) The compromise must be recorded in writing.

Key Takeaway
A compromise on debt between heirs and creditors is valid when the stipulation is that the creditors are absolved and the compromising heir does not recourse against them, based on the principle that making the debtor owner of the debt suffices.

Ruling of Gift: Offer, Acceptance, and Possession
Ruling on gift validity and completion with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three pillars (arkan) of a gift (hibah) according to the Hanafi school and explain why possession (qabd) is necessary for completion and ownership transfer.

Core Idea
A gift is valid with offer and acceptance, but ownership only transfers upon possession.

In this lesson, we examine the fundamental ruling on gifts (hibah) from the Hanafi perspective. The text states that a gift is valid with offer and acceptance, but it is completed and ownership transfers only with possession. This distinction is crucial because without possession, the donor may revoke the gift. We will explore the three integral parts identified by the author and their legal significance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three parts
Read the text and list the three components required for a gift: offer (ījāb), acceptance (qabūl), and possession (qabḍ). Note that the author explicitly states these.
The Arabic text uses 'تصح' (valid) and 'تم' (completed).
2
Understand the continuity argument
The author insists that all three are necessary: without possession, the gift is invalid (bāṭil). This is based on the contractual nature of hibah.
The commentary explains 'hibah is a contract, and no contract is completed without offer and acceptance.'
3
Distinguish validity from completion
Recognize that validity (ṣiḥḥah) occurs with offer and acceptance; completion (tamām) and ownership transfer require possession. Without possession, the gift is not fully effective.
The donee does not become owner until possession occurs.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a donor offers a gift, the donee accepts, but the item remains with the donor. According to the Hanafi ruling, what is the legal status? Answer: The gift is valid but incomplete; ownership has not transferred and the donor may still revoke.
This has practical implications for revocation and inheritance.

[۱۴۹۰] (۱) ہبہ صحیح ہوتا ہے ایجاب اور قبول سے اور پورا ہوتا ہے قبضہ سے۔

اوپر گزر گیا کہ ہبہ عقد ہے اس لئے اس میں قبول کرنے کی ضرورت ہوگی (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن انس قال انفجنا ارنبا بمر الظهران فسعى القوم فلغبوا فادركتها فاخذتها فاتيت بها ابا طلحة فذبحها وبعث الى رسول الله بوركها او فخذيها، قال فخذيها لا شك فيه فقبله قلت واكل منه؟ قال واكل منه ثم قال بعد قبله (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب قبول ہدیۃ الصید ص ۳۵۰ نمبر ۲۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے خرگوش کا گوشت قبول فرمایا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہبہ میں قبول کرنا ضروری ہے (۲) اوپر کی حدیث عائشہ میں تھا کان رسول الله يقبل الهدية ويثيب عليها جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہدیہ میں قبول کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اور تیسرا جز ہے کہ ہبہ پر قبضہ کرے گا یعنی ہبہ پر قبضہ کرے گا تو ہبہ مکمل ہوگا اور موصوبہ بالہ کی ملکیت ہوگی۔ اور قبضہ نہیں کیا تو اس کی ملکیت نہیں ہوگی اور ہبہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔
حاشیہ : ( الف ) اللہ نیکی کرنے سے نہیں روکتا ان لوگوں کے ساتھ جو دین میں تم سے قتال نہیں کرتے اور تم کو گھروں سے نکالتا نہ ہو۔ اور نہ ان کے ساتھ انصاف کرنے سے روکتا ہے، اور اللہ انصاف کرنے والوں کو پسند کرتا ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا ید یہ دو محبت بڑھے گی (ج) حضرت انس فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے مرالظہر ان میں ایک خرگوش دوڑ کر نکل رہا تھا، قوم اس کے پیچھے دوڑی اور اس کو تھکا دیا۔ میں نے اس کو پالیا اور پکڑ لیا ، پس اس کو ابوطلحہ کے پاس لایا۔ انہوں نے اس کو ذبح کیا اور حضور کے پاس اس کی ران بھیجی ، راوی کہتے ہیں کہ کوئی شک نہیں ہے کہ فتنہ ہی بولا۔ میں نے پوچھا حضور نے اس کو کھایا، کہا اس کو کھایا اور اس کو قبول کیا۔
Book of Gift. [1490] (1) Gift is valid with offer and acceptance, and completed with possession. ... Necessary note: Hibah is called giving freely. There is evidence in this verse: 'Allah does not forbid you from being kind and dealing justly with those who have not fought you over religion and have not driven you out of your homes. Indeed, Allah loves those who are just.' (Surah al-Mumtahanah 8). This verse indicates that even with disbelievers, you may deal with kindness and give gifts; Allah does not forbid it, but rather likes it. Imam Bukhari used this verse to argue for giving gifts to polytheists. There is a hadith: 'Aisha said: The Messenger of Allah used to accept gifts and reward for them.' (Bukhari, Chapter on reciprocating gifts, p. 1352, no. 2585). This hadith also proves gift. (2) From Abu Huraira: The Prophet said: 'Exchange gifts, you will love each other.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on encouraging gifts and gifts as a connection between people, vol. 6, p. 280, no. 11946). This hadith also encourages gift. [1490] (1) Gift is valid with offer and acceptance, and completed with possession. For completion, there are three parts. First, the giver makes an offer and gives. It is his property; how can someone take it without giving? So offer is necessary. (2) Gift is a contract, and no contract is completed without offer and acceptance. So offer is necessary. The second part is acceptance. It has passed above that gift is a contract, so acceptance is required. (2) There is indication in hadith: Anas said: 'We startled a rabbit at Marr az-Zahran. The people chased it and got tired. I caught it. I brought it to Abu Talha, who slaughtered it and sent its thigh or hind leg to the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'I have no doubt it was the thigh.' He said: 'He accepted it.' I asked: 'Did he eat from it?' He said: 'He ate from it.' Then he said: 'After acceptance...' (Bukhari, Chapter on accepting a gift of game, p. 350, no. 2572). This hadith shows that the Prophet accepted the rabbit meat, indicating that acceptance is necessary in gift. (2) The earlier hadith of Aisha said: 'The Prophet used to accept gifts and reward for them,' indicating that acceptance is necessary. The third part is that one takes possession of the gift; i.e., if one takes possession, the gift is complete and the donee becomes owner. If possession is not taken, the donee does not become owner, and the gift becomes invalid. Footnote: (a) ... (b) ... (c) ...
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Gift (Kitab al-Hibah) with the fundamental ruling: a gift is valid (ṣaḥīḥ) with offer (ījāb) and acceptance (qabūl), and it becomes complete (tamm) with possession (qabḍ). The commentary explains that 'hibah' means giving something for free. Proof is provided from the Quran (Surah al-Mumtahanah 8: permission to be kind and give gifts even to non-Muslims) and from hadiths (Aisha reporting that the Prophet accepted gifts and rewarded for them, and Abu Huraira reporting the Prophet's encouragement to exchange gifts to increase love). The commentary then breaks down the three integral parts (ajzā') for completion: (1) offer by the giver, (2) acceptance by the donee, and (3) possession by the donee. It argues that offer and acceptance are necessary because hibah is a contract, and all contracts require offer and acceptance. Evidence for acceptance is the hadith of Anas about the Prophet accepting the rabbit meat. Possession is necessary for ownership and completion; without it, the gift is invalid (bāṭil). The footnote provides translations of the cited proofs.

Key Terms
هبة (hibah): A gift; the transfer of ownership of property without compensation.
إيجاب (ījāb): The offer made by the donor expressing the intent to give.
قبول (qabūl): The acceptance by the donee indicating agreement to receive the gift.
قبض (qabḍ): Physical or constructive possession of the gifted item by the donee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is required for a gift to be fully complete and ownership to transfer?
A) Only offer and acceptance.
B) Offer, acceptance, and possession by the donee.
C) Only possession.
D) Offer and possession, but not acceptance.

Key Takeaway
A gift in Hanafi law requires offer and acceptance for validity, but possession is indispensable for ownership transfer and completion.

Proofs of Gift Permissibility and Validity from Quran and Sunnah
Proofs from Quran and Sunnah for gift ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to cite the Quranic verse (Surah al-Mumtahanah 60:8) and two hadiths used to prove the permissibility and validity of gifts in Hanafi fiqh, and explain how each proof supports the ruling.

Core Idea
The Quran permits kindness to all, including gifts; the Prophet accepted gifts, proving acceptance is part of the contract.

In this lesson, we explore the textual evidences for the ruling on gifts. The author cites a Quranic verse and several hadiths to establish both the permissibility of giving gifts and the necessity of acceptance. Understanding these proofs strengthens one's appreciation of how Hanafi scholars derive rulings from primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
Read Surah al-Mumtahanah 60:8 cited in the passage. Identify the words 'birr' and 'qist' which indicate kindness and justice.
Imam Bukhari used this verse to argue for permissibility of giving gifts to non-Muslims.
2
Explain the proof from the Quran
The verse does not directly mention gifts, but it permits birr (kindness) to non-hostile non-Muslims, which includes giving gifts. Hanafis use this as a proof of permissibility (ibahah).
This is an example of dalala zanni (indirect indication).
3
Read the hadith of Aisha
The hadith states that the Prophet used to accept gifts and reward for them. This indicates that acceptance is part of the gift contract and is encouraged.
Acceptance (qabul) is one of the arkan.
4
Read the hadith of Abu Huraira
The Prophet said: 'Exchange gifts, you will love each other.' This encourages the act of giving gifts, establishing the desirability (istihbab) of hibah.
This hadith is used to recommend gifts, not to prove a legal requirement.
5
Read the hadith of Anas
The hadith of the rabbit shows that the Prophet accepted the meat and ate from it. This directly demonstrates the practice of acceptance (qabul) in a gift.
This hadith is a strong proof that acceptance is necessary.

The Gift (Hibah): Validity and Completion
States the ruling that a gift is valid with offer and acceptance and complete with possession, with proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three components of a valid gift (hibah) contract in the Hanafi school and identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah supporting each.

Core Idea
A gift is valid by offer and acceptance, and completed by possession – without possession, ownership does not transfer.

This passage from the text on gifts establishes the foundational ruling: a gift (hibah) is a contract that requires three elements. It also provides the primary textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding these elements is crucial for distinguishing a valid gift from an incomplete one, and for knowing when the donee acquires ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three components of a gift
From the matn 'الهبة تصح بالايجاب والقبول وتم بالقبض', extract the three components: offer, acceptance, and possession.
2
Understand the legal effect of each component
Offer and acceptance make the gift valid (sahih); possession completes it (tamm) and transfers ownership.
Without possession, the donor can revoke the gift.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The verse from Surah al-Mumtahanah 60:8 is cited to prove the permissibility of giving gifts, even to non-Muslims. Imam Bukhari used it for gifts to polytheists.
The verse is general in permissibility.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadith: from Aisha on acceptance and reward, and the rabbit hadith showing the Prophet accepted a gift, proving acceptance is necessary.
The hadith also imply the need for possession.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario, determine if the gift is valid and whether possession has occurred. Then state the hukm.
Practice with examples.

[١٤٩٠] (١) ہبہ صحیح ہوتا ہے ایجاب اور قبول سے اور پورا ہوتا ہے قبضہ سے۔
بہ مکمل ہونے کے لئے تین اجزاء ہیں۔ ایک تو ہبہ کرنے والا ایجاب کرے اور ہبہ کرے۔ اس کا مال ہے، بغیر دیتے ہوئے کوئی کیسے لے سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے ایجاب کرنا ضروری ہے (۲) ہبہ عقد ہے اور کوئی بھی عقد ایجاب اور قبول کئے بغیر پورا نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے ایجاب کرنا ضروری ہے۔ دوسرا جز قبول کرنا۔ اوپر گزر گیا کہ ہبہ عقد ہے اس لئے اس میں قبول کرنے کی ضرورت ہوگی (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن انس قال انفجنا ارنبا بمر الظهران فسعى القوم فلغبوا فادركتها فاخذتها فاتيت بها ابا طلحة فذبحها وبعث الى رسول الله بوركها او فخذيها، قال فخذيها لا شك فيه فقبله قلت واكل منه؟ قال واكل منه ثم قال بعد قبله (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب قبول ہدیۃ الصید ص ۳۵۰ نمبر ۲۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے خرگوش کا گوشت قبول فرمایا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہبہ میں قبول کرنا ضروری ہے (۲) اوپر کی حدیث عائشہ میں تھا كان رسول الله يقبل الهدية ويثيب عليها جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہدیہ میں قبول کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اور تیسرا جز ہے کہ ہبہ پر قبضہ کرے گا یعنی ہبہ پر قبضہ کرے گا تو ہبہ مکمل ہوگا اور موہوب لہ کی ملکیت ہوگی۔ اور قبضہ نہیں کیا تو اس کی ملکیت نہیں ہوگی اور ہبہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔
حاشیہ : ( الف ) اللہ نیکی کرنے سے نہیں روکتا ان لوگوں کے ساتھ جو دین میں تم سے قتال نہیں کرتے اور تم کو گھروں سے نکالتا نہ ہو۔ اور نہ ان کے ساتھ انصاف کرنے سے روکتا ہے، اور اللہ انصاف کرنے والوں کو پسند کرتا ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا آپس میں ہدیہ دو محبت بڑھے گی (ج) حضرت انس فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے مرالظہیران میں ایک خرگوش دوڑ کر نکل رہا تھا، قوم اس کے پیچھے دوڑی اور اس کو تھکا دیا۔ میں نے اس کو پالیا اور پکڑ لیا ، پس اس کو ابوطلحہ کے پاس لایا۔ انہوں نے اس کو ذبح کیا اور حضور کے پاس اس کی ران بھیجی ، راوی کہتے ہیں کہ کوئی شک نہیں ہے کہ فتنہ ہی بولا۔ میں نے پوچھا حضور نے اس کو کھایا، کہا اس کو کھایا اور اس کو قبول کیا۔
This is the Book of Gift. (1490) (1) The gift is valid by offer and acceptance and is completed by possession. Necessary note: Gift means giving for free. Its proof is in this verse: 'Allah does not forbid you from those who do not fight you in religion and do not drive you out of your homes from being righteous and just towards them. Indeed Allah loves those who act justly.' (A) In this verse, it is that even with disbelievers, treat with goodness and kindness and give gifts, Allah does not forbid it but rather likes it. Imam Bukhari deduced from this verse the permissibility of giving gifts to polytheists. In the hadith: 'Aisha said: The Messenger of Allah used to accept gifts and reward for them.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Reward for Gifts, p.1352, no.2585) From this hadith, proof of gift is also established. (2) Narrated by Abu Huraira from the Prophet: 'Give gifts to each other, you will love each other.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Encouragement of Gifts and Presents as a Bond between People, vol.6, p.280, no.11946) From this hadith, encouragement of gift is known. [1490] (1) A gift is valid by offer and acceptance and is completed by possession. For its completion, there are three components. First, the donor makes an offer and gives the gift. It is his property; how can someone take without him giving? So making offer is necessary. (2) Gift is a contract, and no contract is completed without offer and acceptance. So making offer is necessary. The second component is acceptance. It passed above that gift is a contract, so acceptance is needed. (2) There is indication in the hadith: Narrated by Anas: We startled a rabbit at Marr az-Zahran, so the people chased it and became tired, so I caught it and brought it to Abu Talha, who slaughtered it and sent its thigh or its two thighs to the Messenger of Allah. He said: 'Its two thighs, no doubt about it.' The Prophet accepted it. I asked: 'Did he eat from it?' He said: 'He ate from it, then after that he said: He accepted it.' (Bukhari, Chapter on Acceptance of Gift of Game, p.350, no.2572) In this hadith, the Prophet accepted rabbit meat, from which it is known that acceptance in gift is necessary. (2) In the above hadith of Aisha, 'The Messenger of Allah used to accept gifts and reward for them,' from which it is known that acceptance in gift is necessary. And the third component is that he takes possession of the gift, meaning he takes possession of the gift, then the gift is complete and becomes the property of the donee. And if he did not take possession, it will not become his property and the gift will become invalid. Footnote: (A) Allah does not forbid from doing good to those who do not fight you in religion and do not expel you from your homes, and nor from being just to them, and Allah loves those who act justly. (B) The Prophet said: Give gifts to each other, you will increase love. (C) Anas said: We startled a rabbit at Marr az-Zahran, so the people chased it and became tired, so I caught it and brought it to Abu Talha. He slaughtered it and sent its thigh to the Prophet. The narrator said there is no doubt that he said 'its two thighs'. I asked: Did the Prophet eat it? He said: He ate it and accepted it.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the gift (hibah) with its proofs from the Quran and Sunnah. The author begins by stating the core ruling: a gift is valid (sahih) with offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul), and is completed (tamm) by possession (qabd). The Urdu commentary explains that hibah means giving something for free. The proof from the Quran is the verse about being just and good even to disbelievers, which Imam Bukhari used to justify giving gifts to non-Muslims. Then two hadith are cited: the first from Aisha shows the Prophet used to accept gifts and reward for them; the second from Abu Huraira encourages giving gifts to foster love. The commentator then reiterates the three components: offer is necessary because the donor must express the gift; acceptance is necessary because gift is a contract (like sale, it requires both parties' consent); and possession is necessary for completion. The hadith of Anas about the rabbit shows the Prophet accepted the gift, proving the necessity of acceptance. The footnote provides translations of the Arabic texts. This ruling establishes the basic framework of the gift contract in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الهبة (al-hibah): A gift; giving something to another without compensation (i.e., for free).
القبض (al-qabd): Possession; taking physical control of the gifted item.
الإيجاب والقبول (al-ijab wa al-qabul): Offer and acceptance; the two verbal expressions that form the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Acceptance, possession, and monetary consideration

Key Takeaway
A gift in the Hanafi school requires offer and acceptance for validity, but possession (qabd) is essential for its completion and transfer of ownership.

Possession of Gift: In Assembly vs After Separation
Rules on when the donee can take possession: in the assembly without specific permission, but after separation only with renewed permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on when a donee can take possession of a gift: automatically in the assembly, but after separation only with renewed permission from the donor.

Core Idea
The donor's offer implies possession permission only within the session; after separation, renewed permission is needed.

This lesson focuses on a critical timing rule in the Hanafi law of gifts. When a donor makes an offer of a gift, the donee is permitted to take possession in that same assembly without needing explicit permission. However, once the parties separate, that implied permission expires. The donee cannot complete the gift later without a fresh, explicit permission. This rule protects the donor's right to revoke before possession is taken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage contrasts possession taken in the assembly (majlis) vs after separation (iftiraq).
2
Determine the ruling for each
In assembly: permissible (jā'iz) without command. After separation: not valid unless donor explicitly permits again.
The Arabic uses 'jāz' for the first and 'lam tasihh' for the second.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The permission implied in the offer lasts only as long as the session. The session ends when parties separate.
4
Apply the principle to a hypothetical
If donor says 'I gift you these books' and donee takes them immediately, valid. If donee leaves and returns later, needs new permission.
This shows the practical consequence.

[١٤٩١](٢) فان قبض الموهوب له فى المجلس بغير امر الواهب جاز وان قبض بعد الافتراق لم تصح الا ان يأذن له الواهب في القبض
پس اگر موہوب لہ نے قبضہ کیا مجلس میں بغیر واہب کے حکم کے تو جائز ہے۔اور اگر قبضہ کیا افتراق کے بعد تو صحیح نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ ہبہ کرنے والا اس کو اجازت دے قبضہ کرنے کی۔ جس کو ہبہ کیا اس نے قبول کی مجلس میں بغیر ہبہ کرنے والے کی اجازت کے قبضہ کر لیا تو ٹھیک ہے ۔ اور مجلس ختم ہو گئی اس کے بعد موہوب لہ قبضہ کرنا چاہتا ہے تو واہب دوبارہ اجازت دے گا تو قبضہ کر سکے گا۔ اور اگر دوبارہ اجازت نہ دے تو قبضہ کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ اس صورت میں دوبارہ اجازت کی ضرورت ہوگی۔
ایجاب کی مجلس میں ایجاب کرنا ہی قبضہ کرنے کے لئے کافی ہے۔ لیکن مجلس ختم ہوگئی تو ایجاب والی اجازت مجلس ختم ہونے کے ساتھ ختم ہو گئی۔ اس لئے اب قبضہ کے لئے دوبارہ اجازت کی ضرورت ہوگی۔
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ ایجاب کی اجازت مجلس تک رہتی ہے اور مجلس ختم ہونے پر وہ اجازت ختم ہو جاتی ہے۔
(1491) (2) If the donee takes possession in the assembly without the command of the donor, it is permissible. And if he takes possession after separation, it is not valid unless the donor permits him to take possession. So if the donee took possession in the assembly without the permission of the donor, it is fine. And if the session ended and after that the donee wants to take possession, then the donor will give permission again, then he can take possession. And if the donor does not give permission again, then taking possession is not correct. In this case, renewed permission is needed. In the session of offer, making the offer itself is sufficient for taking possession. But when the session ended, the permission attached to the offer ended with the end of the session. Therefore, now for possession, renewed permission is needed. The principle: this issue is based on the principle that the permission of the offer lasts only until the session, and when the session ends, that permission ends.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage states a subsidiary ruling regarding the timing of possession (qabd) in a gift. The author clarifies: If the donee takes possession of the gifted item in the same assembly (majlis) where the offer was made, even without explicit permission from the donor, it is permissible (jā'iz). The reasoning is that the donor's offer inherently implies permission to take possession in that session. However, if the parties separate (iftirāq) after the offer and acceptance, the donee cannot take possession later without a new, explicit permission from the donor. The session's implied permission expires with the session. The underlying principle is that permission associated with an offer is limited to the duration of the session. This rule prevents the gift from being completed without the donor's ongoing consent, protecting the donor's right to revoke before possession.

Key Terms
المجلس (al-majlis): The session or meeting where the offer and acceptance of the gift take place. It is the timeframe during which the contract is formed.
الافتراق (al-iftiraq): Separation; the termination of the session, either by physical departure or by ending the discussion.

Key Terms from Source Passage
