C) The donee needs two witnesses to confirm the offer.
D) The donee must pay a token amount to complete the gift.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, possession of a gift must occur in the same session as the offer, or the donor must give explicit permission later.

Gift Contract Formation and Revocability before Compensation
Gift contract formation and revocability rules with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the formation of a gift contract and identify when a gift becomes irrevocable, contrasting it with the Maliki position.

Core Idea
A gift is formed by offer and acceptance but ownership only transfers upon possession; the donor can revoke before compensation.

The gift (hiba) is a gratuitous transfer that, in Hanafi fiqh, does not transfer ownership until possession (qabd) occurs. Moreover, even after possession, the donor retains the right to revoke if no compensation ('iwad) was given. This lesson explores the ruling and its proof, including a key dispute with Imam Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract formation
Recognize that a gift contract is concluded (tun'aqid) by the donor's words like 'I gave' (وهبت). Offer and acceptance create a valid contract, but it is incomplete for ownership transfer.
2
Understand the role of possession
Possession (qabd) is a condition (shart) for ownership to pass to the donee. Before possession, the donor remains owner and may revoke. This is supported by statements of Companions.
Companions: Umar, Uthman, Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas, Muadh, Shurayh.
3
Learn the revocability rule
Even after possession, the donor can take back the gifted item if the donee gave nothing in return (compensation) and the item is still in the donee's possession. The hadith 'الواهب احق بهبته مالم يثب منها' proves this.
Compensation (‘iwad) makes the gift irrevocable.
4
Contrast the Maliki position
Imam Malik holds that ownership transfers upon acceptance, just like in sale. The Hanafi school distinguishes gift from sale due to its gratuitous nature, requiring possession for ownership.
This difference has practical effects on inheritance and revocability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١٤٩٢] (٣) وتنعقد الهبة بقوله هبة کے بدلے کچھ آتا نہیں ہے اس لئے موہوب لہ کے قبضہ سے پہلے واہب کی ہی ملکیت ہوگی اس لئے وہ انکار کر سکتا ہے(۲) اثر میں ہے کہ قبضہ سے پہلے موہوب لہ کی ملکیت نہیں ہوگی۔ عن ابی موسی اشعری قال قال عمر بن الخطاب الانحال ميراث مالم يقبض وعن عثمان وابن عمر وابن عباس قالوا لا تجوز صدقة حتى تقبض وعن معاذ بن جبل وشريح انهما كانا لا يجيز انها حتى تقبض (الف) ( سنن بیھقی ، باب شرط القبض في الهبة ، ج سادس ص ۲۸۱، نمبر ۱۱۹۵۱) ان اقوال میں ہے کہ قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے موہوب لہ کی ملکیت نہیں ہوگی بلکہ اگر واہب مر گیا تو اس کے ورثہ میں تقسیم ہوگی (۳) بلکہ ہبہ کا معاملہ تو اتنا کمزور ہے کہ قبضہ کرنے کے بعد اگر موہوب لہ نے ہبہ کے بدلے واہب کو کچھ نہیں دیا اور ہبہ کی چیز بعینہ موہوب لہ کے پاس ہے تو ہبہ کی چیز موہوب لہ سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرۃ قال قال رسول الله الواهب احق بهبته مالم يثب منها (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب البيوع ج ثالث ص ۳۹ نمبر ۲۹۵۲ سنن بیھقی ، باب المكافاة فی الهبة ج سادس ص ۱۸۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہبہ کی چیز پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے موہوب لہ کی ملکیت نہیں ہوگی ۔ انده امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ قبول کے بعد قبضہ سے پہلے بھی موہوب لہ کی ملکیت ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے بیع میں قبول کے بعد مشتری کی ملکیت ہو جاتی ہے، چاہے ابھی قبضہ نہ کیا ہو۔
(1492) (3) The gift is contracted by his saying: [I gave, I gifted, I donated, etc.] Since nothing comes in return for the gift, therefore before possession of the donee, ownership remains with the donor, so he can revoke. (2) There is an effect that before possession, the donee does not have ownership. From Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'Gifts are inherited as long as they are not taken possession.' And from Uthman, Ibn Umar, and Ibn Abbas, they said: 'A charity is not valid until it is taken possession.' And from Muadh ibn Jabal and Shurayh, they both used not to validate gifts until they were taken possession. (A) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Condition of Possession in Gift, vol.6, p.281, no.11951) In these sayings, it is that before possession, the donee does not have ownership; rather if the donor dies, it will be distributed among his heirs. (3) Rather, the transaction of gift is so weak that after possession, if the donee gave nothing in return to the donor and the gifted item is still in the possession of the donee, the donor can take back the gifted item. There is a hadith: from Abu Huraira, the Prophet said: 'The donor has more right to his gift as long as he is not rewarded for it.' (B) (Dar Qutni, Book of Sales, vol.3, p.39, no.2952; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Reward for Gift, vol.6, p.181) From this hadith, it is known that before possession, the donee does not have ownership. Meanwhile, Imam Malik says that after acceptance, even before possession, the donee becomes the owner, just as in sale after acceptance the buyer becomes owner even if he hasn't taken possession yet.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage discusses the formation and revocability of a gift contract. The author states that the contract is formed by the donor saying words like 'I gave' (وهبت). Since it is gratuitous, ownership does not transfer until possession, and the donor can revoke before possession. The text then cites a number of Companions (Umar, Uthman, Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas, Muadh, Shurayh) who all assert that a gift is not valid without possession; if the donor dies before possession, it returns to the donor's estate. After possession, the gift is still weak: the donor can take it back if the donee has not given something in return (compensation), and the item is still in the donee's possession. The hadith of the Prophet: 'The donor has more right to his gift as long as he is not rewarded for it' supports this revocability. The passage concludes with an inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Malik holds that once acceptance occurs, ownership transfers before possession, analogizing to a sale (where ownership transfers upon contract, not possession). The Hanafi position insists on possession for ownership transfer, emphasizing the gift's gratuitous nature.

Key Terms
تنعقد (tun'aqid): The gift contract is formed or concluded. It becomes a legally recognized contract upon the pronouncement of offer and acceptance.
يثب (yuthib): To reward or compensate the donor for the gift. Literally 'he is rewarded'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dispute mentioned in this lesson, what is the difference between Imam Malik and the Hanafi school regarding the transfer of ownership in a gift?
A) Malik says ownership transfers upon offer; Hanafi says upon acceptance.
B) Malik says ownership transfers upon acceptance; Hanafi says upon possession.
C) Malik says ownership transfers upon possession; Hanafi says upon acceptance.
D) Malik says ownership never transfers; Hanafi says it transfers immediately.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a gift contract is formed by offer and acceptance, but ownership only transfers upon possession; the donor retains the right to revoke until compensation is given.

Possession in the Gift Assembly and Its Effect
Ruling with proof on possession timing in gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for possession in the gift assembly and explain why possession after separation requires renewed permission.

Core Idea
Possession in the gift assembly transfers ownership; after separation, the donor's implied permission expires.

This passage clarifies a key condition for completing a gift in Hanafi fiqh: the timing of possession. The donor's offer implies permission to take possession only during the gathering. If the donee delays, the permission lapses, and a new explicit permission is needed. The author supports this with Companion statements and a hadith, and contrasts the Hanafi view with Imam Malik's analogical reasoning from sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its two scenarios
Note the Hanafi position: possession in the assembly is valid without explicit permission; possession after separation is invalid unless the donor gives new permission.
This distinction hinges on the concept of implied permission (izn dimni) from the offer.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites athar from 'Umar, 'Uthman, Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and Shurayh that a gift is not valid until possessed, and the hadith 'الواهب احق بهبته' from Abu Hurairah.
These are primarily ahad hadith and Companion statements, giving zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah of the hadith
The phrase 'أحق بهبته' implies the donor retains superior entitlement until recompense, indicating ownership does not fully transfer without possession or recompense.
This is a mafhum (implied meaning) that possession is a condition for completion.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam Malik holds that acceptance alone transfers ownership, analogizing gift to sale. The Hanafi response is that a gift is gratuitous and weaker, so it requires possession.
The practical difference (thamarah) appears if the donor dies before possession: Hanafi returns gift to estate, Maliki gives it to donee.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, supported by the explicit hadith and Companion practice, and by istihsan (juristic preference) that considers the weakness of gift contracts.
The assembly-based rule is an instance of istihsan overriding strict qiyas (which would require permission for every possession).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴۹۱](۲) فان قبض الموهوب له فى المجلس بغير امر الواهب جاز وان قبض بعد الافتراق لم تصح الا ان يأذن له الواهب في القبض (۲) اثر میں ہے کہ قبضہ سے پہلے موہوب لہ کی ملکیت نہیں ہوگی۔ عن ابی موسی اشعری قال قال عمر بن الخطاب الانحال ميراث مالم يقبض وعن عثمان وابن عمر وابن عباس قالوا لا تجوز صدقة حتى تقبض وعن معاذ بن جبل وشريح انهما كانا لا يجيز انها حتى تقبض (الف) ( سنن بیھقی ، باب شرط القبض في الحبة ، ج سادس ص ۲۸۱، نمبر ۱۱۹۵۱) ان اقوال میں ہے کہ قبضہ کرنے للبیھقی ، سے پہلے موہوب لہ کی ملکیت نہیں ہوگی بلکہ اگر واہب مر گیا تو اس کے ورثہ میں تقسیم ہوگی (۳) بلکہ ہبہ کا معاملہ تو اتنا کمزور ہے کہ قبضہ کرنے کے بعد اگر موہوب لہ نے ہبہ کے بدلے واہب کو کچھ نہیں دیا اور ہبہ کی چیز بعینہ موہوب لہ کے پاس ہے تو ہبہ کی چیز موہوب لہ سے واپس لے سکتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرۃ قال قال رسول الله الواهب احق بهبته مالم يثب منها (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب البيوع ج ثالث ص ۳۹ نمبر ۲۹۵۲ سفن سیھتی ، باب المكافاة فی البتہ ج سادس ص ۱۸۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہبہ کی چیز پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے موہوب لہ کی ملکیت نہیں ہوگی ۔ انده امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ قبول کے بعد قبضہ سے پہلے بھی موہوب لہ کی ملکیت ہو جائے گی۔ جیسے بیع میں قبول کے بعد مشتری کی ملکیت ہو جاتی ہے، چاہے ابھی قبضہ نہ کیا ہو۔ [۱۴۹۱) (۲) پس اگر موہوب لہ نے قبضہ کیا مجلس میں بغیر واہب کے حکم کے تو جائز ہے۔اور اگر قبضہ کیا جا ئیگی کے بعد تو صیح نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ ہبہ کرنے والا اس کو اجازت دے قبضہ کرنے کی۔ جس کو ہبہ کیا اس نے قبول کی مجلس میں بغیر ہبہ کرنے والے کی اجازت کے قبضہ کر لیا تو ٹھیک ہے ۔ اور مجلس ختم ہو گئی اس کے بعد موہوب لہ قبضہ کرنا چاہتا ہے تو واہب دوبارہ اجازت دے گا تو قبضہ کر سکے گا۔ اور اگر دوبارہ اجازت نہ دے تو قبضہ کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ اس صورت میں دوبارہ اجازت کی ضرورت ہوگی۔ ایجاب کی مجلس میں ایجاب کرنا ہی قبضہ کرنے کے لئے کافی ہے۔ لیکن مجلس ختم ہوگئی تو ایجاب والی اجازت مجلس ختم ہونے کے ساتھ ختم ہو گئی۔ اس لئے اب قبضہ کے لئے دوبارہ اجازت کی ضرورت ہوگی۔
[1491](2) If the donee takes possession in the assembly without the command of the donor, it is permitted. If he takes possession after separation, it is not valid unless the donor permits him for possession. (2) In the tradition: Ownership of the donee does not occur before possession. From Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'Gifts become inheritance as long as possession has not been taken.' From 'Uthman, Ibn 'Umar, and Ibn 'Abbas: they said: 'A sadaqah is not valid until it is possessed.' From Mu'adh ibn Jabal and Shurayh: they used to not validate it until it is possessed. (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on condition of possession in gift, vol. 6, p. 281, no. 11951) In these statements: ownership of the donee does not occur before possession, rather if the donor dies, it will be distributed among his heirs. (3) Rather the transaction of gift is so weak that after taking possession, if the donee does not give anything in return to the donor and the thing given remains with the donee in its original state, the donor can take it back. In the hadith: from Abu Huraira: the Messenger of Allah said: 'The donor is more entitled to his gift as long as he has not been recompensed for it.' (b) (Darqutni, book of sales, vol. 3, p. 39, no. 2952; Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter of recompense in gift, vol. 6, p. 181) From this hadith it is understood that ownership of the donee does not occur before taking possession of the gifted item. And Imam Malik says that after acceptance, even before possession, the donee becomes owner, just as in sale the buyer becomes owner after acceptance even if possession is not taken. [1491] (2) So if the donee took possession in the assembly without the donor's command, it is valid. And if he took possession after the gathering ended, it is not valid unless the donor gives him permission for possession. The person to whom the gift is given took possession in the assembly of acceptance without the permission of the donor, it is correct. And after the assembly ends, if the donee wishes to take possession, the donor will give permission again, then he can take possession. And if he does not give permission again, possession is not valid. In this case, renewed permission is needed. The ijab (offer) in the assembly of ijab is sufficient for taking possession. But when the assembly ends, the permission given with the ijab ends with the end of the assembly. Therefore, renewed permission is needed for possession.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the effect of taking possession in a gift contract. The author states the Hanafi position: if the donee takes possession of the gifted item during the same gathering (majlis) in which the gift was offered, even without the donor's explicit permission, the possession is valid and the gift is complete. However, if the donee delays possession until after the parties have separated, the possession is not valid unless the donor gives new permission. This is because the implied permission granted by the offer (ijab) is considered to extend only for the duration of the gathering. After separation, that implied permission lapses, and a fresh explicit permission is required. The author supports this with athar (traditions) from the Companions, such as 'Umar, 'Uthman, Ibn 'Umar, and Ibn 'Abbas, who stated that a gift is not effective until possession is taken. Then a hadith from Abu Hurairah is cited: 'The donor is more entitled to his gift as long as he has not been recompensed for it,' indicating that ownership does not transfer until possession occurs. The commentator also notes a disagreement with Imam Malik, who considers acceptance alone sufficient for ownership transfer, analogous to a sale contract. This is an example of istihsan in Hanafi fiqh, where the weakness of the gift contract (compared to sale) requires possession for completion.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession of the gifted item, which is a condition for the completion of the gift contract according to Hanafi fiqh.
مجلس (majlis): The gathering in which the gift offer (ijab) is made; also referred to as the 'assembly of contract'.
موهوب له (mawhub lahu): The donee, the recipient of the gift.
واهب (wahib): The donor, the person who gives the gift.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing, the gift is valid automatically.
B) The donee must pay the donor a token amount.
C) The donor must give renewed permission for possession.
D) The gift must be re-offered and accepted.

Key Takeaway
Possession in the assembly completes the gift without explicit permission; after separation, the donor's permission must be renewed.

Phrases That Constitute a Valid Gift
Enumeration and proof of seven expressions for concluding a gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven valid expressions for concluding a gift (hibah) in Hanafi fiqh and state the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
A gift is validly concluded by any of seven specific phrases; each is proven by authentic hadith.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a gift contract (hibah) depends on the offer (ijab) being expressed using recognized terms. This lesson enumerates the seven expressions that are established by the Sunnah, along with their supporting evidence. Understanding these phrases is essential for correctly concluding a gift and avoiding invalid transactions.

Guided Path
1
List the seven phrases
From the text, extract the seven phrases: وهبت, نحلت, أعطيت, أطعمتك, جعلت, أعمرتك, حملتك.
These are the standard expressions recognized by the Hanafi school.
2
Classify each phrase
Note which phrases are direct (وهبت, نحلت, أعطيت) and which are context-specific (أطعمتك for food, جعلت for made garment, أعمرتك for life gift, حملتك for mounting).
The specific phrases imply a gift in their respective contexts.
3
Associate each with its hadith evidence
Link each phrase to the hadith cited in the text: نحلت (Bukhari 2586), أعمرتك (Muslim 1625), حملتك (Bukhari 2636), etc.
The hadith demonstrate that the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions used these words for gifts.
4
Understand the ruling on 'umra'
The phrase 'أعمرتك' (giving for life) is considered an absolute gift in Hanafi fiqh, not a temporary grant, based on the hadith of Jabir.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from some other schools.

Commentary
This passage is a definition and enumeration of the valid expressions (sighah) for concluding a gift contract. The author lists seven phrases, and then provides proofs from hadith for each. These phrases are: (1) وهبت (wahaba): clear word for gift; (2) نحلت (nahala): granting, supported by the hadith of Nu'man ibn Bashir where the Prophet said 'ارجعه'; (3) أعطيت (a'tayta): giving, used interchangeably with هبة; (4) أطعمتك (at'amtuka): specifically for food, because food is consumed; (5) جعلت (ja'altu): making something for someone, indicating ownership; (6) أعمرتك (a'martuka): giving for life, which according to hadith becomes a complete gift and not a temporary grant; (7) حملتك (hamaltuka): mounting on a riding animal, which can mean either temporary loan or complete gift depending on intention. The author supports each with Islamic legal sources, particularly hadith. This lesson is a memorization anchor for students to know which words effect a gift.

Key Terms
نحلة (nuhlah): A grant or gift, synonymous with hibah in the context of concluding a gift.
عمرى (umra): A gift for life, which becomes an absolute gift according to Hanafi fiqh, not a temporary grant.
هبة (hibah): The gift contract itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A gift is validly concluded by any of seven established expressions; the intention of gift and subsequent possession complete the contract.

Seven Valid Expressions for Hibah (Gift)
Listing of seven Arabic phrases that effect a valid hibah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven expressions that effect a valid hibah, explain the proof for each, and apply the Hanafi rule that any clear expression of gift with delivery suffices.

Core Idea
Any clear expression indicating immediate transfer of ownership effects a valid hibah, even if not the word 'hibah'.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a gift (hibah) depends on a clear expression of transferring ownership without compensation. The author of our text enumerates seven Arabic sentences that accomplish this, each illustrated with proof from the Sunnah or customary usage. Understanding these expressions helps you recognize a valid gift in both classical and modern contexts, and appreciate that the law looks to substance over form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven expressions
Read the passage and list the seven Arabic phrases the author gives: wahaba, nahala, a'ta, at'ama for food, ja'ala with 'laka', a'mara (umra), and hamala (mounting). Note that the author explains each with proof.
The seventh phrase 'hamaltuka' has two possible meanings; intention determines if it is a gift or a loan.
2
Examine the proofs (dalil)
For each expression, locate the proof provided. The main proofs are hadith: the hadith of Nu'man ibn Bashir for 'nahala', the hadith of Jabir for 'umra', and the hadith of 'Umar for 'hamala'. Other expressions rely on common usage or linguistic implication.
The hadith of Nu'man is from Bukhari; it shows the Prophet accepted the word 'nahaltu' as a valid gift expression.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
For each hadith, identify how the wording proves the expression is valid. The key is that the Prophet did not object to the words themselves; only the lack of equality among children was criticized. This implies the expression itself is acceptable.
The hadith of 'Umar on giving a horse in charity shows that 'hamala' can mean complete transfer, not just temporary use.
4
Distinguish between clear and ambiguous expressions
Some expressions are explicit (e.g., 'wahaba'), while others like 'hamaltuka' require intention. Learn the nuance: if the speaker intends a permanent gift, it is valid; if only temporary loan, it is not a hibah. Intention (niyyah) plays a role.
The Hanafi school accepts any wording that clearly indicates a gift, even if not purely Arabic or standard, as long as the meaning is unambiguous.
5
Summarize the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi position is that hibah is effected by any expression, in any language, that indicates immediate transfer of ownership without compensation. These seven are examples, not an exhaustive list. The proof is the general principle from hadith and the absence of restriction in the sources.
This contrasts with schools like the Shafi'i, which may require specific wording (e.g., 'hibah' or 'tamlik').

یہ بتلانا چاہتے ہیں کہ کن کن جملوں سے ہبہ کا انعقاد ہو جاتا ہے۔ جس کے لئے مصنف نے سات جملے استعمال کئے ہیں۔ ہر جملہ کی تصریح اور دلیل پیش خدمت ہے (۱) و هیت کا جملہ ہبہ کے لئے صریح ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے ہبہ منعقد ہو جائے گا (۲) نحلت کے جملہ سے بھی بہ منعقد ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن نعمان بن بشیر ان اباه اتی به الی رسول الله الله فقال اني نحلت ابنى هذا غلاما فقال اكل ولدك نحلت مثله قال لا قال فارجعه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب المكافات في البتة ص ۳۵۲ نمبر ۲۵۸۶) اس حدیث میں محلت کے جملہ سے لڑکے کو ہبہ کیا ہے ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ محلت کے لفظ سے ہبہ منعقد ہوتا ہے (۳) اعطیت کا جملہ بھی ہبہ کرنے کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے، لوگ کہتے ہیں اعطاك الله و هیک اللہ کے معنی میں (۴) کھانے کے بارے میں کہتے ہیں اطعمتك هذا الطعام تو ہبہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کھانا کھانے میں عین شی، ہلاک ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس جملہ سے عین کھانے کا مالک بنانا ہوا۔ اس لئے اس جملہ سے بھی کھانے کا ہبہ کرنا ثابت ہوگا (۵) جعلت هذا الثوب لک میں لفظ لک ملکیت کے لئے آتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے بھی ہبہ ثابت ہو جائے گا (۶) اعمر تك هذا الشيء سے بھی ہیہ ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے کہ کوئی اعمر عمری له ولعقبه کہے تو اگر چہ عمری کے معنی عمر بھر کا ہے لیکن اس سے وہ چیز مکمل اس کے ہاتھ سے چلی جائے گی اور جس کے لئے عمر بھر کے لئے دی اس کے ورثہ میں وہ چیز تقسیم ہوگی۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله ان رسول الله الله قال ايما رجل اعمـر عمـرى له ولعقبه فانها للذى اعطيها لا ترجع الى الذى اعطاها لانه اعطى عطاء وقعت فيه المواريث (ب) ( مسلم شریف ، باب العمری ص ۳۷ نمبر ۱۶۲۵) اس حدیث میں لفظ عمری ہبہ کے معنی میں استعمال ہوا ہے (۷) حملک علی هذه الدابة کے دو معنے ہیں ایک یہ کہ وقتی طور پر عاریت کے طور پر اس جانور کو سواری کے لئے آپ کو دے رہا ہوں۔ اور دوسرے معنی ہیں کہ مکمل اس جانور کو آپ کو حوالے کر رہا ہوں اور ہبہ کر رہا ہوں۔ اس لئے اگر دوسرے معنی کی نیت کی تو دوسرا معنی ملحوظ ہونگے۔ اور اس جملہ سے ہبہ کا انعقاد ہو جائے گا۔ لوگ حمل الامیر فلانا علی فرس بولتے ہیں اور اس سے مراد لیتے ہیں کہ امیر نے فلاں کو گھوڑا مکمل دے دیا اور ہبہ کر دیا ۔ اس لئے اس جملے سے بھی گھوڑے کا ہبہ ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے، حملت على فرس فی سبیل اللہ سے پورا گھوڑا صدقہ کرنا مرا دلیا گیا ہے۔ قال عمر حملت على فرس في سبيل الله فرأيته يباع فسألت رسول الله الله فقال لا تشتروه ولا تعد فی صدقتک (بخاری شریف، باب اذا احمل رجل علی فرس فھو کا لعمری و الصدقۃ ص ۳۵۹ نمبر ۲۶۳۶) اس حدیث میں حمل على فرس بول کر پورے گھوڑے کا صدقہ مراد لیا گیا ہے۔ حاشیه : (الف) حضرت بشیر حضور کے پاس آئے اور کہا میں نے اس بیٹے کو غلام ہبہ کیا ہے۔ آپ نے پوچھا آپ نے اور بیٹے کو اسی طرح غلام ہبہ کیا ہے؟ کہا نہیں۔ آپ نے فرمایا پھر یہ واپس کرلو (ب) آپ نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی عمری کرے تو وہ چیز اس کے لئے ہوگی۔ اور اس کے بعد والوں کے لئے ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے لئے ہے جس کو دیا۔ وہ دینے والے کی طرف واپس نہیں آئے گی۔ اس لئے کہ ایسا عطیہ دیا جس میں وراثت جاری ہوگی۔
You gifted, you bestowed, you gave, I fed you this food, I made this garment for you, I granted you lifelong usufruct. This cloth is made for you, for your whole life this thing is given to you, you are mounted on this riding animal if the intention is gift by mounting. In this passage, the author intends to explain which sentences effect a hibah. For this, the author uses seven sentences. Each sentence's clarification and proof is presented: (1) The sentence 'wahaba' is explicit for gift, so hibah is concluded by it. (2) The sentence 'nahaltu' also concludes hibah; its proof is the hadith from Nu'man ibn Bashir that his father brought him to the Prophet and said 'I bestowed upon this son of mine a slave,' and the Prophet asked 'Did you bestow similarly to all your children?' He said no, so the Prophet said 'Take it back.' (Bukhari) So it is known that 'nahaltu' effects hibah. (3) The sentence 'a'taytu' is also used for giving; people say 'a'taka Allah' meaning 'gave you'. (4) Regarding food, one says 'at'amtu ka hadha al-ta'am' so it is hibah because food is consumed, so by this sentence one owns the food. (5) 'Ja'altu hadha al-thawba laka' where 'laka' indicates ownership, so hibah is established. (6) 'A'martuka hadha al-shay' also effects hibah because there is a hadith: if one says 'a'martu umra li wa li'aqibihi' then even though 'umra' means for life, the thing goes completely from his hand and becomes inheritable. Hadith from Jabir: 'Any man who grants a life grant to someone and his descendants, it belongs to the one given it and does not return to the giver, because it is a gift that falls into inheritance.' (Muslim) So 'umra' is used in the sense of hibah. (7) 'Hamaltuka 'ala hadhihi al-dabbah' has two meanings: one is temporary loan (ariyah) for riding; the second is complete transfer as hibah. If the second meaning is intended, then hibah is concluded. People say 'hamala al-amiru fulanan 'ala farasin' meaning the amir gave him a horse completely. There is also a hadith: 'Umar said: I gave a horse in charity in the way of Allah, then I saw it being sold, so I asked the Prophet, and he said: Do not buy it and do not take back your charity.' (Bukhari) In this hadith, 'hamala 'ala farasin' is used meaning complete charity. Footnote: (a) Hadith of Bashir; (b) Hadith of Jabir on umra.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author lists seven Arabic sentences that effect a valid hibah (gift) according to the Hanafi school. The first, 'wahaba', is explicit. The second, 'nahaltu', is supported by the hadith of Nu'man ibn Bashir where the Prophet used this word. The third, 'a'taytu', is commonly used. The fourth, 'at'amtu', specifically for food, grants ownership because food is consumed. The fifth, 'ja'altu... laka', where 'laka' indicates ownership. The sixth, 'a'martu', referring to 'umra' (life grant), is shown by the hadith of Jabir to be a full gift, not a temporary usufruct. The seventh, 'hamaltuka', has two possible meanings: temporary loan or permanent gift. If the intention is the latter, it is valid. The hadith of 'Umar about giving a horse confirms that 'hamala' can mean a complete transfer. Each proof is from authentic hadith, establishing the ruling firmly.

Key Terms
هبة (hibah): A gift; the transfer of ownership of a specific property without compensation, made voluntarily during one's lifetime.
نحل (nahl): A gift, often used for a parental gift to a child; synonymous with hibah in this context.
عمرى ('umra): A life grant; a gift of property for the recipient's lifetime, which becomes full ownership by Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following phrases is considered a valid expression for a hibah (gift)?
A) 'I loan you this car.'
B) 'I bestow (nahaltu) upon you this house.'
C) 'I will give you this watch tomorrow.'
D) 'I invite you to dinner.'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a hibah through any clear expression of immediate ownership transfer, exemplified by seven specific Arabic phrases, as supported by authentic hadith and the principle of intention.

Hibah of Undivided Divisible Property: The Hanafi Requirement of Separation
Hanafi ruling on hibah of musha' divisible property with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hibah of undivided divisible property, explain the condition of separation and delivery, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument with its Hanafi response.

Core Idea
A gift of an undivided divisible share is invalid until physically separated and delivered.

Giving a gift seems straightforward, but what if the property is shared and not physically divided? The Hanafi school requires that the gifted portion be separated and delivered for ownership to transfer. This lesson dives into the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, exploring the proofs and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: hibah of musha' in divisible property is not valid (ghayr ja'iz) until the share is physically separated, delivered, and free from encumbrances.
The author's statement: "Hibah is not permissible in divisible things unless they are free from rights and divided."
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hibah of undivided divisible property is valid without separation, relying on the hadith of Hawazin and the drink hadith.
The Shafi'i position contrasts directly with the Hanafi condition.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze each Shafi'i dalil: (1) The Prophet gave undivided booty to the captives of Hawazin; (2) The Prophet allowed a boy to retain his share of a drink without division.
These appear to show permissibility of gifting undivided property.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes each proof: the Hawazin incident was a return of property to original owners, not a gift; the drink hadith involved a boy who was the sole owner of his share, not co-ownership.
Thus the proofs are limited to their specific contexts and do not abrogate the general requirement of delivery.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if someone gifts a share of a house without separating it, the Hanafi school deems the gift invalid until division, whereas the Shafi'i school validates it immediately.
The Hanafi ruling aims to prevent future disputes over undefined shares.

نہ کیا گیا ہو۔ علیحدہ نہ کیا گیا ہو۔ اور جان پہچان کے لئے نشان نہ لگا دیا گیا ہو (۲) عن ابن شبرمة قال ان لم يجز كل واحد منهما ما وهب له صاحبه فليس بشيء (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب حيازة ما وهب احدهما يقبض للطفل ابوه ، ج سادس ، ص ۲۸۲، نمبر ۱۱۹۵۳) جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہبہ اس وقت نہیں ہے جب تک کہ اس کو حقوق ، ابوہ، سے الگ نہ کر دے۔ جائیگی۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ شی ، موہوب کو اپنے حصے سے الگ نہ والمقسومة وغير المقسومة ص ۳۵۴ نمبر ۲۶۰۳) که قبیلہ ہوازن کے لوگوں کو صحابہ نے قید کیا تھا اور ان سے مال غنیمت حاصل کی تھی۔ پھر وہ تمام کو قبیلہ ہوازن کی طرف واپس کیا۔ حالانکہ واپس کرتے وقت غنیمت اور قیدی مشترک تھے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغیر تقسیم شدہ بھی ہبہ کر سکتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن سهل بن سعد ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اتى بشراب وعن يمينه غلام وعن يساره اشياخ فقال للغلام اتأذن لى ان اعطى هؤلاء فقال الغلام لا والله لا اوثر بنصیبی منک احدا فتله في يده (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الحبة المقبوضة وغير المقبوضة والمقسومة وغير المقسومة ص ۳۵۴ نمبر ۲۶۰۵) اس حدیث میں شراب اور حاشیہ: (الف) حضرت عمر بن عبد العزیز نے لکھا کہ ہبہ جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ اس کو الگ کیا جائے اور علیحدہ کیا جائے اور پہچان کے لئے نشان لگایا جائے (ب) ابن شہر مہ نے کہا کہ جو کچھ ہبہ کیا گیا وہ ایک دوسرے سے الگ نہ کیا گیا ہو تو کچھ بھی نہیں ہے یعنی ہیہ درست نہیں ہو گا ( ج ) جو کچھ ہوازن سے غنیمت میں ملا تھا حضور اور صحابہ نے ان کو ہبہ کیا جو تقسیم شدہ نہیں تھا (ج) حضور کے پاس شربت لایا گیا اور آپ کی دائیں جانب لڑکا تھا اور بائیں جانب بڑے بوڑھے تھے تو لڑکے سے کہا، کیا اجازت دیتے ہو کہ ان لوگوں کو دوں۔ تو لڑکے نے کہا نہیں۔ خدا کی قسم آپ کی جانب سے حصے کو کسیکو ترجیح نہیں دوں گا، پس اس کے ہاتھ میں دے دیا۔
This thing and I mounted you on this riding animal if he intended the mounting as a gift. [1493] (4) And it is not permissible. [1493] (4) Hibah is not permissible in divisible things unless they are free from rights and divided. The following issues revolve around this: the donee must take complete possession of the gifted item for ownership; otherwise not. For complete possession, if the thing is shared but divisible, it must be divided and free from others' debts and rights. Then the donee's possession is considered complete. So the author said: In what can be divided, hibah is not valid unless free from rights and divided. Its proof is the athar of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: 'He wrote that hibah is not permissible except what is separated, singled out, and made known.' (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). In this athar, hibah is not valid until it is separated. (2) From Ibn Shubruma: 'If each of them does not take possession of what was gifted to him, it is nothing.' (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). This shows that if the gifted thing is not taken possession, there is no possession. (3) In Sunan al-Bayhaqi, the saying of Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'No gift is valid from a child unless separated from the parent.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). From this it is known that hibah is not valid until separated. Imam Shafi'i holds that even if the gifted thing is not separated from the giver's share and not divided, the donee still owns it. His proof is the hadith: 'The Prophet and his companions gave to the captives of Hawazin what they had taken from them, while it was undivided.' (c) (Bukhari). This shows that hibah can be made without division. (2) Another hadith from Sahl ibn Sa'd: 'The Prophet was brought a drink, with a boy on his right and elders on his left. He said to the boy: Do you allow me to give to these? The boy said: No, by Allah, I will not give anyone preference over my share from you, so he put it in his hand.' (Bukhari). Footnotes: (a) Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote that hibah is not valid unless separated, singled out, and marked. (b) Ibn Shubruma said: If what is gifted is not separated from each other, it is nothing, i.e., the hibah is not valid. (c) What was taken from Hawazin as booty, the Prophet and companions gave it back, and it was not divided. (d) The hadith about the drink.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position, stated by the author, is that a hibah of a divisible undivided property (musha') is not valid until the gifted portion is physically separated and delivered to the donee, and free from any encumbrances. The proof includes the practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, the statement of Ibn Shubruma, and the saying of Umar ibn al-Khattab. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the Prophet gave undivided booty to the captives of Hawazin, proving that division is not necessary for validity. The Hanafi response, implied by the author's inclusion of the proofs, is that the Hawazin incident was a special case of returning what was already in their possession, not a typical hibah. The Hanafi ruling aims to prevent ambiguity and ensure complete transfer of possession, which is essential for ownership in hibah.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking control of the gifted item. For hibah, qabd is a condition for ownership to transfer.
مشاع (musha'): Undivided, shared property where each co-owner's share is not physically separate.
قسمة (qismah): Physical division of jointly owned property into separate shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for a hibah of a divisible undivided property to be valid?
A) The gift must be witnessed by two witnesses.
B) The gifted share must be physically separated and delivered to the donee.
C) The donee must pay a nominal price.
D) The donor must declare the intention three times.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi requirement of physical separation for hibah of divisible undivided property ensures complete possession and prevents future disputes.

Gift in Divisible Property Requires Isolation and Division
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gifts of undivided shares in divisible property, identify the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i school, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
A gift of an undivided share in divisible property is invalid in the Hanafi school until physically separated and divided.

Gifting a share of something you own in common can be tricky. The Hanafi school sets a clear condition: if the property is divisible, the gifted share must be physically separated and handed over. The Shafi'i school disagrees, citing the Prophet's own example. This lesson unpacks the proofs on both sides and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: a gift of an undivided share in divisible property is invalid (fasid) unless the share is physically isolated and divided.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
The Shafi'i school holds the gift is valid even without division. Their evidence: the Prophet gifted undivided spoils to the tribe of Hawazin and gave a drink from a shared vessel to one person.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis argue those hadith involve collective gifts or indivisible items. They rely on athar (precedent) from ‘Umar ibn ‘Abd al-‘Aziz, Ibn Shubruma, and ‘Umar ibn al-Khattab requiring separation.
In Hanafi usul, specific athar can override general hadith.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, the donee does not own the share until divided; under Shafi'i, the donee becomes co-owner immediately.
5
Understand the tarjih
The Hanafi view is relied upon because the athar directly address the issue of divisible property and are more specific than the general practice in the hadith.

Book of Gift: This thing and I mounted you on this animal if he intended by the mounting the gift [1493] (4) And a gift is not permissible in divisible property except if it is isolated and divided. [1493] (4) It is not permissible to give a gift in divisible things except that they are free from rights and have been divided. The following few issues depend on this: that the donee must take complete possession of the gifted item, then his ownership will be established, otherwise not. And for complete possession, the rule is that if the item is shared but can be divided, then it must be divided. And it must be free from the debts and rights of others, then the donee's possession will be considered complete. Therefore, the author said that in a thing that can be divided, a gift is not permissible unless it is free from rights and divided. Its proof is an athar. ‘Umar ibn ‘Abd al-‘Aziz wrote that no gift is permissible except that which is isolated, separated, and marked (a) (Musannaf ‘Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Nahl, vol. 9, p. 104, no. 16514). This athar indicates that the item is not permissible until it is separated, not separated, and a mark is made for identification. (2) From Ibn Shubruma, he said: If each of them does not take possession of what his companion gifted him, it is nothing (b) (Musannaf ‘Abd al-Razzaq, Bab Hiyazat ma Wahab Ahaduhuma li-Sahibihi, vol. 9, p. 16, no. 16570). This athar also shows that if the gifted item is not isolated, there is no possession. (3) In Sunan al-Bayhaqi, ‘Umar ibn al-Khattab said: There is no gift that is valid from a child without the father (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Yaqbidu li’l-Tifl Abuhu, vol. 6, p. 282, no. 11953). From this it is known that a gift is not valid until it is separated from the rights of others. According to Imam al-Shafi‘i, even if he does not separate the gifted item from his share and does not divide it, the donee still owns it. His proof is this hadith: The Prophet ﷺ and his Companions gifted to the tribe of Hawazin what they had taken as spoils from them while it was undivided (c) (Bukhari, Bab al-Hibbah al-Maqbudah wa Ghayr al-Maqbudah wa’l-Maqsumah wa Ghayr al-Maqsumah, p. 354, no. 2603). That is, the Companions had captured the people of Hawazin and obtained spoils from them. Then they returned all of them to the tribe of Hawazin, even though at the time of return the spoils and captives were shared. From this it is understood that a gift can be given without division. (2) In a hadith: From Sahl ibn Sa‘d that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was brought a drink, and on his right was a boy and on his left were elderly people. He said to the boy, 'Do you permit me to give to these?' The boy said, 'No, by Allah, I will not give preference to anyone over my share from you,' so he placed it in his hand (c) (Bukhari, Bab al-Hibbah al-Maqbudah wa Ghayr al-Maqbudah wa’l-Maqsumah wa Ghayr al-Maqsumah, p. 354, no. 2605). In this hadith, the drink and... Footnotes: (a) Hadrat ‘Umar ibn ‘Abd al-‘Aziz wrote that a gift is not permissible unless it is separated, isolated, and marked for identification. (b) Ibn Shubruma said: What was gifted, if it is not separated from each other, then nothing, meaning the gift is not valid. (c) What was received as spoils from Hawazin, the Prophet and the Companions gifted it while it was undivided. (d) A drink was brought to the Prophet and on his right was a boy and on his left were elderly people, so he said to the boy, 'Do you permit me to give to these?' The boy said, 'No, by Allah, I will not give preference to anyone over my share from you,' so he gave it to him.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position is that a gift of an undivided share in divisible property is invalid unless the gifted item is physically separated and divided. The author provides three proofs from the actions and statements of early Muslims: (1) The letter of ‘Umar ibn ‘Abd al-‘Aziz requiring isolation and marking, (2) The statement of Ibn Shubruma that taking possession is necessary, and (3) The statement of ‘Umar ibn al-Khattab that a gift from a child without the father's involvement is invalid, implying the need for separation. The Shafi‘i school argues that such a gift is valid even without division, citing the hadith of Hawazin where the Prophet gifted undivided spoils and the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa‘d where a drink was given to a specific person without division. The Hanafi response, implicitly, is that those cases involve either gifts to a group (which is permissible collectively) or items that are indivisible by nature. The athar (reports from companions and early authorities) contradict the generality of the hadith, and the Hanafi school gives precedence to these specific precedents. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that if someone gifts half a house to a person without dividing, the gift is invalid in the Hanafi school, but valid in the Shafi‘i school.

Key Terms
مشاع (musha‘): Undivided share in a jointly owned property
محوزة (mahuzah): Isolated, taken possession separately

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is a gift of half of a house (which is divisible) valid without separating the portion?
A) Yes, valid.
B) No, invalid unless separated and divided.
C) Valid only if the house is small.
D) Valid if the donee is a relative.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a gift of an undivided share in divisible property is invalid unless physically separated and divided.

Gift of Undivided Share in Indivisible Property Permissible
Ruling with proof that gift of undivided share in indivisible property is valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between divisible and indivisible property and state the Hanafi ruling on gifting an undivided share in each.

Core Idea
Gifting an undivided share is valid only if the property cannot be divided without ruining its use.

This lesson examines a key exception in Hanafi gift law: while a gift of an undivided share in divisible property is invalid without physical separation, the opposite holds for indivisible items. You will learn why a shared bathroom can be gifted as a whole, and how the hadith of Abu Qatadah provides the proof for this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the gift (hiba) of an undivided share (musha‘) in property that cannot be divided (la yuqsam). The ruling is ja’iz (permissible and valid).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Abu Qatadah, where the Prophet ﷺ permitted the collective gift of a wild donkey’s meat to the Companions without division.
Reference: Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab man istawhaba min ashabihi shay’an, hadith no. 2570.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that division is not required for a gift when the property is indivisible. The meat could not be divided without difficulty, so the Prophet allowed the undivided gift, establishing the principle.
The illa (reason) is the prevention of hardship and waste.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant intra-Hanafi disagreement on this ruling; it is muttafaq alayh within the school.
5
Evaluate the practical application
Apply the rule to real examples: a bathhouse, a shared well, or a small room. If the property cannot be partitioned without destroying its utility, the gift of a share is valid and possession is given by whatever means possible.
For divisible property, the rule remains that the gift of an undivided share is fasid unless the property is divided and delivered.

Source Text

ر جو چیز تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتی مثلا حمام اور غسل خانہ جو تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتا ہو اور وہ تقسیم کرنے سے کسی کام کا نہیں رہے گا اس کو بغیر تقسیم کئے بھی ہبہ
کرنا جائز ہے۔ جو چیز تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتی اور تقسیم کرنے سے وہ کسی کام کی نہیں رہے گی۔ اس کو ہبہ میں تقسیم کرنے کی شرط لگا ئیں گے تو وہ چیز ضائع ہو جائے گی۔اس لئے اس کے قبضے کے لئے جتنا ممکن ہو سکا اتنا ہی کریں گے۔ اور تقسیم کی شرط نہیں لگے گی (۲) حضرت ابو قتادہ نے وحشی گدھا شکار کر کے سب صحابہ کو مشتر کہ ہبہ کیا۔ اس کو تقسیم کر کے ہبہ نہیں کیا اور حضور نے اس کو جائز قرار دیا۔ کیونکہ تقسیم کر کے گوشت پکا نا مشکل تھا۔ اس لئے مشترکہ ہبہ ہی جائز قرار دیا گیا۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن ابي قتادة السلمى عن ابيه ... فشددت على الحمار فعقرته ثم جئت به وقد مات فوقعوا فيه يأكلونه ثم انهم شكوا في اكلهم اياه وهم حرم (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب من استوهب من اصحابہ شیئا ص نمبر ۲۵۷۰) اس حدیث میں سب صحابہ کو مشترکہ طور گدھے کا گوشت ہبہ کیا گیا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو چیز تقسیم نہ ہو سکتی ہو اس کو مشتر کہ ہبہ کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ او پر بھی کئی احادیث مشتر کہ ہبہ کی گزری۔
[1494] (5) And the gift of an undivided share in what is not divisible is permissible. [1395] (2) And whoever gifts an undivided share, the gift is void; then if he divides it and hands it over, it becomes valid. The water was not divided, yet it was gifted to all. From this it is known that even a divisible thing can be gifted while undivided. [1394] (5) And a gift of a shared thing that cannot be divided is permissible. For example, a bathhouse or a washroom that cannot be divided and if divided becomes useless, it is permissible to gift it without division. For a thing that cannot be divided and if division is made a condition, it will be wasted. Therefore, for its possession, we will do as much as possible and the condition of division will not be applied. (2) Hadrat Abu Qatadah hunted a wild donkey and gifted it to all the Companions collectively. He did not gift it after dividing it, and the Prophet ﷺ declared it permissible. Because dividing the meat would have made cooking difficult. Therefore, the collective gift was deemed permissible. A part of the hadith is: From ‘Abdullah ibn Abi Qatadah al-Sulami from his father... Then I attacked the donkey and hamstrung it, then I brought it while it was dead, and they fell upon it eating it, then they complained about eating it while they were in ihram (a) (Bukhari, Bab man istawhaba min ashabihi shay’an, p. no. 2570). In this hadith, the meat of the donkey was gifted to all Companions collectively. From this it is known that it is permissible to gift collectively that which cannot be divided. And several other hadith about collective gifts have also passed.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that if the gifted property is indivisible (i.e., cannot be divided without destroying its utility), then a gift of an undivided share is valid. Examples include a bathhouse or a small washroom that becomes useless if divided. The condition of division is not required for possession; whatever physical possession is possible suffices. The proof is the hadith of Abu Qatadah, where the Prophet allowed the collective gift of a wild donkey’s meat to the Companions even though it was not divided, because dividing the meat would have caused difficulty. This indicates that for indivisible items, the requirement of division is waived. The commentary also references other similar hadith.

Key Terms
مشاع (musha‘): Undivided share in a jointly owned property
لا يقسم (la yuqsam): Indivisible, cannot be divided without loss of utility

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a gift that is valid even if given as an undivided share?
A) Half of a house that can be partitioned.
B) A shared bathroom.
C) Half of a piece of land.
D) A garden divided by a fence.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a gift of an undivided share in property that cannot be divided without destroying its utility is valid and does not require physical separation.

Gift of Undivided Share in Divisible Property Invalid Without Division
Ruling with proof on gift of undivided share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gifting an undivided share in divisible property and explain how it can become valid through subsequent division and delivery.

Core Idea
Gift of an undivided share is initially void, but becomes valid if divided and delivered before possession.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in gifts: giving a part of jointly owned property without specifying the portion. The Hanafi school holds that such a gift is invalid unless the property is first divided and the specific share handed over. We will examine the ruling, its basis, and the conditions that rectify it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
The act is gifting an undivided share in divisible property. The Hanafi ruling is that the gift is initially fasid (voidable) because the share is not specified.
Fasid means the contract is valid in essence but lacks a condition that can be fulfilled later.
2
Understand the condition for validity
The gift can become valid if the donor subsequently divides the property and delivers the specific share to the donee. The key condition is that at the time of possession, the gifted item must be divided.
If division and delivery occur after the contract, the gift becomes valid as per the text.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The text cites an athar (narration) from Ibn Shubruma: specifying a fraction (e.g., third or quarter) requires division, whereas specifying a specific amount (e.g., 100 dinars) does not. This supports the need for division.
The dalil is from Musannaf ‘Abd al-Razzaq, showing early Hanafi reliance on such reports.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi‘i school holds that a gift of an undivided share is valid even without division. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
The Hanafi position is based on the condition of division, while Shafi‘is do not require it.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
For example, two heirs own a house jointly. One wants to gift his share. According to Hanafi, he must first physically divide the house (e.g., assign specific rooms) and then deliver that portion. Otherwise the gift is fasid.
This applies to divisible properties; indivisible properties like a car may be treated differently.

[۱۴۹۵] (۶) اگر ہبہ کیا مشترک چیز کا کچھ حصہ تو ہبہ فاسد ہے۔ پس اگر اس کو تقسیم کر دیا اور سپر د کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ شرق مشترک چیز کو اوپر کے آثار کی بنا پر تقسیم کر کے ہبہ کرنا چاہئے ۔ لیکن بغیر تقسیم کئے ہوئے ہی ہبہ کر دیا تو ہبہ فاسد ہو گا۔ لیکن اگر بعد میں تقسیم کر کے موہوب لہ کو قبضہ دے دیا تب بھی جائز ہو جائے گا۔
اصل یہ ہے کہ قبضہ کرتے وقت ہبہ کی چیز تقسیم شدہ ہونی چاہئے۔ چاہے اس سے پہلے تقسیم شدہ نہ ہو۔ اس لئے قبضہ کرتے وقت چیز کو تقسیم کر کے دے دیا تو ہبہ جائز ہو جائے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ سألت ابن شبرمة عنه فقال اذا سمى فجعل له مائة دينار من ماله فهو جائز وان سمى ثلثا او ربعا لم يجز حتى يقسمه (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الصبات ج تاسع ص ۱۰۸ نمبر ۱۶۵۳۱) اس اثر میں اشارہ ہے کہ تقسیم کر دے تو یہ جائز ہو جائے گا۔
قبضہ کے وقت بھی تقسیم نہیں کرے گا تو ہبہ فاسد ہی رہے گا۔
شقصا : ایک حصہ۔ مشاعا : مشترک۔
[1495] (6) If a part of a shared thing is gifted, then the gift is void. Then if he divides it and hands it over, it becomes valid. It is appropriate to gift a shared thing after dividing it, based on the previous evidences. But if he gives it without dividing, the gift is void. However, if later he divides it and gives possession to the donee, then it becomes valid. The principle is that at the time of possession, the gifted item must be divided, even if it was not divided before. Therefore, if at the time of possession he divides the item and gives it, the gift becomes valid. (2) There is proof in an athar: I asked Ibn Shubruma about it, and he said: If he specifies and makes for him one hundred dinars from his wealth, it is valid. But if he specifies a third or a quarter, it is not valid until he divides it (b) (Musannaf ‘Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Sibat, vol. 9, p. 108, no. 16531). This athar indicates that if he divides, it becomes valid. If he does not divide even at the time of possession, the gift remains void. Shiqsa: a share. Musha‘a: shared.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It clarifies that if someone gifts an undivided share (shiqs musha‘) in divisible property, the gift is initially fasid (voidable). However, it can be rectified if the donor subsequently divides the property and hands the specific portion over to the donee. The key principle is that at the time of possession (qabd), the item must be divided. This is supported by the athar of Ibn Shubruma: if one specifies a lump sum like one hundred dinars, the gift is valid; but if one specifies a fraction like a third or a quarter, it is not valid until divided. This indicates that division and specification are necessary for validity. If possession occurs without division, the gift remains fasid and does not transfer ownership.

Key Terms
شقص (shiqs): A share or portion of a property
مشاع (musha‘): Undivided, shared without physical demarcation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone gifts half of a house (divisible) without dividing it, the gift is initially fasid. How can it become valid?
A) By the donee taking possession immediately.
B) By the donor later dividing the house and handing over the specific half.
C) By the donor saying 'I gift half' repeatedly.
D) It can never become valid.

Key Takeaway
A gift of an undivided share in divisible property is fasid unless the property is divided and the specific share is delivered to the donee.

beginner
10 min
Gift of Divisible vs Indivisible Property
States two foundational rules for valid gift transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rules for valid gift transfer based on property divisibility and apply them to new scenarios involving mushāʿ.

Core Idea
Divisible property requires divided possession; indivisible property accepts undivided possession.

In the Hanafi school, the validity of a gift (hibah) depends on whether the gifted property can be divided without losing utility. If the property is divisible, the donee must take possession after physical division. If it is indivisible, a gift of an undivided share (mushāʿ) is valid without prior division. This lesson examines these two rules and their proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of property
Recognize that the passage divides property into divisible (e.g., land, grain) and indivisible (e.g., bathhouse, narrow lane) based on whether division destroys utility.
Indivisible items are those that become useless when split.
2
State the rule for divisible property
A gift of divisible property is not valid unless the donee takes possession after the property has been physically divided (maḥūzah maqsūmah).
The condition is exclusive possession of a separated portion.
3
State the rule for indivisible property
A gift of an undivided share (mushāʿ) in indivisible property is valid without prior division, because dividing would render it useless.
The condition of division is waived; possession is taken as much as possible.
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith of Abu Qatada's wild donkey (Bukhari) shows the Prophet (peace be upon him) approved a shared gift of meat without division, establishing the validity of mushāʿ gifts in indivisible items.
The meat was indivisible for immediate cooking, so division was not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الهبة
الهبة فيما يقسم لا تجوز إلا محوزة مقسومة وهبة المشاع فيما لا يقسم جائزة
[۱۳۹۴ (۵) اور مشترک کا ہبہ اس چیز کا جو تقسیم نہ ہو سکتی ہو جائز ہے۔
ر جو چیز تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتی مثلا حمام اور غسل خانہ جو تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتا ہو اور وہ تقسیم کرنے سے کسی کام کا نہیں رہے گا اس کو بغیر تقسیم کئے بھی ہبہ کرنا جائز ہے۔ جو چیز تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتی اور تقسیم کرنے سے وہ کسی کام کی نہیں رہے گی۔ اس کو ہبہ میں تقسیم کرنے کی شرط لگا ئیں گے تو وہ چیز ضائع ہو جائے گی۔اس لئے اس کے قبضے کے لئے جتنا ممکن ہو سکا اتنا ہی کریں گے۔ اور تقسیم کی شرط نہیں لگے گی (۲) حضرت ابو قتادہ نے وحشی گدھا شکار کر کے سب صحابہ کو مشتر کہ ہبہ کیا۔ اس کو تقسیم کر کے ہبہ نہیں کیا اور حضور نے اس کو جائز قرار دیا۔ کیونکہ تقسیم کر کے گوشت پکا نا مشکل تھا۔ اس لئے مشترکہ ہبہ ہی جائز قرار دیا گیا۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن ابي قتادة السلمى عن ابيه ... فشددت على الحمار فعقرته ثم جئت به وقد مات فوقعوا فيه يأكلونه ثم انهم شكوا في اكلهم اياه وهم حرم (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب من استوهب من اصحابہ شیئا ص نمبر ۲۵۷۰) اس حدیث میں سب صحابہ کو مشترکہ طور گدھے کا گوشت ہبہ کیا گیا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو چیز تقسیم نہ ہو سکتی ہو اس کو مشتر کہ ہبہ کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ او پر بھی کئی احادیث مشتر کہ ہبہ کی گزری۔
Book of Gifts. A gift of what can be divided is not valid unless it is possessed as divided, and a gift of undivided property in what cannot be divided is valid. [1394 (5)] And the gift of shared property that cannot be divided is valid. For something that cannot be divided, e.g., a bathhouse or washroom that cannot be divided and would become useless if divided, it is valid to gift it without division. If one stipulates division in the gift of something that cannot be divided, it would be wasted. Therefore, for possession, one does as much as possible and the condition of division does not apply. (2) Sayyiduna Abu Qatada hunted a wild donkey and gifted it to all the Companions as shared. He did not divide it before gifting, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared it valid because dividing the meat for cooking was difficult. Thus the shared gift was deemed valid. A portion of the hadith: From Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada as-Sulami from his father: ... I attacked the donkey and hamstrung it, then brought it when it had died, and they fell upon it eating it. Then they expressed doubt about eating it while they were in ihram. (Bukhari, Chapter: Whoever Asked His Companions for Something, no. 2570). This hadith shows that the Companions were given the donkey meat as a shared gift, proving that a gift of something indivisible as shared is valid. Other hadiths on shared gifts have also passed.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Hibah (Book of Gifts) by stating the foundational ruling on the validity of gifts based on the nature of the property. The matn (core text) presents two rules: (1) A gift of divisible property (i.e., something that can be divided without loss) is not valid unless the donee takes possession after the property has been physically divided. (2) A gift of undivided property (musha') in something that cannot be divided (e.g., a bathhouse, a narrow lane, or a large building) is valid without prior division. The Urdu commentary explains the rationale: if dividing the item would destroy its utility, the condition of division is waived, and possession is taken as much as possible. The commentator provides a hadith from Bukhari where the Prophet (peace be upon him) validated a shared gift of a wild donkey to the Companions by Abu Qatada, even though the meat was not divided. This serves as proof (dalil) that shariah permits shared gifts of indivisible items. The passage thus establishes a key distinction in Hanafi gift law between divisible and indivisible property.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushāʿ): Undivided share of a jointly owned property, where each owner's portion is not physically separated.
محوزة مقسومة (maḥūzah maqsūmah): Possessed after being physically divided; the donee must take exclusive possession of a separated portion of the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a valid gift of undivided property (mushā') without prior division?
A) A 30% share in a land that can be split into two farms
B) A 50% share in a shop with separate rooms
C) A 20% share in a public bathhouse that cannot be divided
D) A 10% share in a car that can be driven away

Key Takeaway
For a valid gift, divisible property requires divided possession; indivisible property accepts undivided possession.
